      <p><br> This page holds approved <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYKTN#nominate" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYKTN">nominations</a> that are waiting to appear in the "<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DYK">Did you know</a>" section on the <a href="/wiki/Main_Page" title="Main Page">Main Page</a>. Following DYK approval, nominations are processed and moved into a <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">Prep area</a>, and from there, prep sets are promoted to a queue, and then to the main page. </p>
      <p>To create a new nomination or to see those that are yet to be approved, see <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know" title="Template talk:Did you know">Template talk:Did you know</a>. For the discussion page see <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">WT:DYK</a>. Click on the link to go directly to the <a href="#Special_occasion_holding_area">Special occasion holding area</a>. </p> 
      <ul>

      </ul>

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Instructions_for_nominators">Instructions for nominators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-1" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>This page is for those nominations that have already been approved and are waiting to be promoted. If yours has been approved but has not yet been run on the main page, it should either be on this page or will soon be moved here, or already promoted to a <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">Prep area or Queue</a> ahead of an appearance on the main page. </p>
      <p>If you wish to create a new nomination, please go to the <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know" title="Template talk:Did you know">Template talk:Did you know</a> page; there are instructions there in a section similar to this one on how to nominate an article for DYK. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequently_asked_questions">Frequently asked questions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-2" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Backlogged.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Backlogged?">Backlogged?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-3" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>This page is often backlogged. As long as your submission is still on the page, it will stay there until someone promotes it to a preparation area. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Where_is_my_hook.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Where_is_my_hook?">Where is my hook?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-4" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>If you can't find the nomination you submitted to the <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Did_you_know" title="Template talk:Did you know">nominations</a> page, and it also isn't on this page, in most cases it means your article has been approved and is either in one of the <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue#Prep_areas" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">prep areas</a>, has been promoted from prep to a <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue#Queues" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">queue</a>, or is on the main page. </p>
      <p>If the nominated hook is in none of those places, then the nomination has probably been rejected. Such a rejection usually only occurs if it was at least a couple of weeks old and had unresolved issues for which any discussion had gone stale. If you think your nomination was unfairly rejected, you can query this on the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">DYK discussion page</a>, but as a general rule such nominations will only be restored in exceptional circumstances. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Instructions_for_other_editors">Instructions for other editors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-5" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_promote_an_accepted_hook">How to promote an accepted hook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-6" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Did_you_know/Preparation_areas" title="Wikipedia:Did you know/Preparation areas">Wikipedia:Did you know/Preparation areas</a> for full instructions. Note that there are discussions currently under way for changing this process; if any changes are made, these instructions will be revised as necessary.</li> 
       <li>In one window, open the DYK nomination subpage of the hook you would like to promote.</li> 
       <li>In another window, open the <b><a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know/Queue#Prep_areas" title="Template:Did you know/Queue">prep set</a></b> you intend to add the hook to.</li> 
       <li>In the prep set... 
        <ul>
         <li>Paste the hook into the hook area (be sure to not paste in <i>that that</i>)</li> 
         <li>Paste the credit information (<span class="nowrap">{{DYKmake}}</span> and/or <span class="nowrap">{{DYKnom}}</span>) into the credits area.</li> 
         <li>Add an edit summary, e.g., "Promoted [[Jane Fonda]]", preview, and save</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Back on DYK nomination page... 
        <ul>
         <li>change <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>{{DYKsubpage</code></span> to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code>{{<b>subst:</b>DYKsubpage</code></span></li> 
         <li>change <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code class="nowrap" style="">|passed=</code></span> to <span class="example" style="font-family: Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', serif; color: #006400;"><code class="nowrap" style="">|passed=yes</code></span></li> 
         <li>Add an edit summary, e.g., "Promoted original hook to Prep 3", preview, and save</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="How_to_remove_a_hook_from_the_prep_areas_or_queue">How to remove a hook from the prep areas or queue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved/top&amp;action=edit&amp;section=T-7" title="Edit section: ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>Edit the prep area or queue where the hook is and remove the hook and the credits associated with it.</li> 
       <li>Go to the hook's nomination subpage (there should have been a link to it in the credits section). 
        <ul>
         <li>View the edit history for that page</li> 
         <li>Go back to the last version <i>before</i> the edit where the hook was promoted, and revert to that version to make the nomination active again.</li> 
         <li>Add a new icon on the nomination subpage to cancel the previous tick and leave a comment after it explaining that the hook was removed from the prep area or queue, and why, so that later reviewers are aware of this issue.</li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li>Add a transclusion of the template back to the <a href="/wiki/T:TDYK" class="mw-redirect" title="T:TDYK">nominations page</a> so that reviewers can see it. It goes under the date that it was first created/expanded/listed as a GA. You may need to add back the day header for that date if it had been removed from the nominations page.</li> 
       <li>If you removed the hook from a queue, it is best to either replace it with another hook from one of the prep areas, or to leave a message at <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:DYK" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia talk:DYK">WT:DYK</a> asking someone else to do so.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h1><span class="mw-headline" id="Nominations">Nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Approved_nominations">Approved nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Approved nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_April_23"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_April_23">Articles created/expanded on April 23</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on April 23">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="James_Fulton_Zimmerman">James Fulton Zimmerman</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJames_Fulton_Zimmerman&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=James_Fulton_Zimmerman&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... <s>that <b><a href="/wiki/James_Fulton_Zimmerman" title="James Fulton Zimmerman">James Fulton Zimmerman</a></b> was the first historian to study U.S. State Department records on the controversial <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">impressment</a> that occurred just before the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> was declared?</s> — <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://scholarshare.temple.edu/bitstream/handle/20.500.12613/4048/TETDEDXWolf-temple-0225E-12189.pdf?sequence=1&amp;isAllowed=y">Wolf, 2015, p. 20</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li>Comment: Statement and source supporting hook is found in the 2nd paragraph of the <a href="/wiki/James_Fulton_Zimmerman#Career" title="James Fulton Zimmerman"><i>Career</i></a> section.</li> 
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Conn_Findlay" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Conn Findlay">Template:Did you know nominations/Conn Findlay</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Gwillhickers" title="User:Gwillhickers">Gwillhickers</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gwillhickers" title="User talk:Gwillhickers">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 23:40, 25 April 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Gwillhickers" title="User:Gwillhickers">Gwillhickers</a>:</span> I started to review this nomination, and still want to. But I think you need to work on the wording of the first half of the hook and where it's mentioned in the article. It's too close to the exact wording of the source: "He was the first historian to study U.S. State Department records on impressment ... " Let me know, and I'll get back to this. <a href="/wiki/User:Maile66" title="User:Maile66">— Maile </a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Maile66" title="User talk:Maile66">talk</a>) 18:21, 20 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul> 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <dl>
             <dd>
              <ul>
               <li>The phrase in question in the source reads: <i>was the first historian to study U.S. State Department records</i>. This is a general statement, however, will this variation work?:</li>
              </ul>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>ALT1:</b> ... that <b><a href="/wiki/James_Fulton_Zimmerman" title="James Fulton Zimmerman">James Fulton Zimmerman</a></b> proved to be the first historian to examine U.S. State Department records on the controversial <a href="/wiki/Impressment" title="Impressment">impressment</a> that occurred just before the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> was declared?<br>-- <a href="/wiki/User:Gwillhickers" title="User:Gwillhickers"><i>Gwillhickers</i></a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gwillhickers" title="User talk:Gwillhickers">talk</a>) 19:45, 20 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_April_26"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_April_26">Articles created/expanded on April 26</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on April 26">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Time_in_Kiribati">Time in Kiribati</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FTime_in_Kiribati&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Time_in_Kiribati&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Time_in_Kiribati" title="Time in Kiribati">Kiribati</a></b> observes three <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zones</a>, including <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B14:00" title="UTC+14:00">UTC+14:00</a>, which as the earliest time zone in the world makes Kiribati one of the first countries to celebrate a <a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.cia.gov/the-world-factbook/countries/kiribati/">[1]</a> </small></s></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <ul>
           <li><b>ALT1</b>: ... that between 1979 and 1994 the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> were a <b><a href="/wiki/Time_in_Kiribati" title="Time in Kiribati">full day ahead</a></b> of Kiribati's eastern <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/australiaandthepacific/samoa/8980665/Samoa-prepares-to-skip-Dec-30.html">[2]</a> </small></li>
          </ul></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Though this may be a more niche subject, I believe it is certainly quite fascinating.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <p><b>Overall</b>: <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Anonymous_7481" title="User:Anonymous 7481">Anonymous 7481</a>:</span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/the-world-factbook/countries/kiribati/">The source</a> doesn't say anything about "which as the earliest time zone in the world makes Kiribati one of the first countries to celebrate a <a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a>" (it should be "to celebrate <a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a>", BTW). Personally, I know the hook is true as every New Year news broadcast mention it, and because of that, I think the fact "that the Gilbert Islands were a full day ahead of the eastern islands [...] When the Republic of Kiribati was founded in 1979" is even more interesting, especially because they lived like that for 24 years. What do you think? Of course, the hook would need to be reworked to be meaningful. Also, I left a few maintenance tags. <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CC-BY-SA" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:CC-BY-SA">(CC)</a> <a href="/wiki/User:Tbhotch" title="User:Tbhotch"><span style="color:#4B0082;">Tb</span><span style="color:#6082B6;">hotch</span></a><sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Tbhotch" title="User talk:Tbhotch"><span style="color:#555555;">™</span></a></sup> 17:22, 7 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMarie-Adolphine&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>

      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Franciscan_Missionaries_of_Mary" title="Franciscan Missionaries of Mary">Franciscan Missionaries of Mary</a>; <b><a href="/wiki/Marie-Adolphine" title="Marie-Adolphine">Marie-Adolphine</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, <b><a href="/wiki/Marie-Hermine_of_Jesus" title="Marie-Hermine of Jesus">Marie-Hermine of Jesus</a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Maria_Chiara_Nanetti" title="Maria Chiara Nanetti">Maria Chiara Nanetti</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Marie_de_la_Paix_Giuliani" title="Marie de la Paix Giuliani">Marie de la Paix Giuliani</a></b> became <a href="/wiki/Martyr_Saints_of_China" title="Martyr Saints of China">Martyr Saints of China</a> when they were canonised in 2000? <small>Sources include <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://fmm.org/saints-and-blessed/">"The seven Franciscan Missionaries of Mary were: Marie-Hermine Grivot, Marie de Ste. Nathalie Kerguin, Marie de St. Just Moreau, Marie de la Paix Giuliani, Maria Chiara Nanetti, Marie Amandine Jeuris, Marie Adolphine Dierk. They were beatified by Pope Pius XII in 1946 and canonized on October 1, 2000 in Rome by Pope John Paul II."</a></small>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_2"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_2">Articles created/expanded on May 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Michael_George_Levy">Michael George Levy</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMichael_George_Levy&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Michael_George_Levy&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that despite not identifying as Jewish, <b><a href="/wiki/Michael_George_Levy" title="Michael George Levy">Michael George Levy</a></b> was denied a <a href="/wiki/Military_Cross" title="Military Cross">Military Cross</a> due to his commanding officer's anti-Semitic views? <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.lookoutnewspaper.com/forgotten-hero-forgotten-war/According">to Edwards, and multiple accounts from other PPCLI veterans, after catching wind of Lt Levy’s remarkable efforts, PPCLI commanding officer Lieutenant-Colonel Jim Stone declared “I will never award a medal to a Jew.” Instead of Levy receiving a Military Cross for his role in the victory, a medal was awarded to the Commander of D Company headquarters... Levy’s son, Ottawa-based accountant Don Levy says he and his family are still perplexed by reports of Col Stone’s comments, since neither he nor his siblings or their parents ever identified as being Jewish.</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that after escaping from a Japanese internment camp, <b><a href="/wiki/Michael_George_Levy" title="Michael George Levy">Michael George Levy</a></b> was trained in guerrilla warfare and sent to the jungles of Malaya? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://espritdecorps.ca/battle-of-kapyong/2016/5/9/the-spirit-of-a-solider">Under cover of darkness, Michael and four British internees escaped from Lunghua camp on May 22, 1944 and set off for India... Once in India, Michael was recruited by the British Army’s elite Special Operations Executive (SOE), and...dropped behind enemy lines in the Malayan jungle</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kapyong" title="Battle of Kapyong">Battle of Kapyong</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Michael_George_Levy" title="Michael George Levy">Michael George Levy</a></b> ordered an artillery bombardment of his own position? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://espritdecorps.ca/battle-of-kapyong/2016/5/9/the-spirit-of-a-solider">During the 1951 Battle of Kapyong, while under heavy attack, Lt. Levy initiated and personally directed the artillery bombardment from his Platoon’s position on the ground onto this location</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Ali_Akbar_Aboutorabi_Fard" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Ali Akbar Aboutorabi Fard">Template:Did you know nominations/Ali Akbar Aboutorabi Fard</a></li>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_7"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_7">Articles created/expanded on May 7</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Pre-Raphaelites">American Pre-Raphaelites</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FAmerican_Pre-Raphaelites&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=American_Pre-Raphaelites&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/American_Pre-Raphaelites" title="American Pre-Raphaelites">American Pre-Raphaelite</a></b> painters had an obsession with depicting birds' nest <a href="/wiki/Still_life" title="Still life">still lifes</a>? <small>Source: "It would appear more than coincidental that the emphasis upon informal stilllife elements, the accidental, humble object found in nature, precisely, meticulously rendered, began to appear in American art at just the time when the first major show of English painting was presented to the American public. Moreover, we have noted the profusion of Bird's Nest subjects in American painting after this time." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://doi.org/10.2307%2F1593877">[3]</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/American_Pre-Raphaelites" title="American Pre-Raphaelites">American Pre-Raphaelites</a></b> rebuked <a href="/wiki/Albert_Bierstadt" title="Albert Bierstadt">Albert Bierstadt</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rocky_Mountains,_Lander%27s_Peak" title="The Rocky Mountains, Lander's Peak">The Rocky Mountains, Lander's Peak</a></i> by saying "20 times the study&nbsp;... would not have justified him in attempting to fill so large a canvas"? <small>Source: "Six years later, The Rocky Mountains, Lander's Peak was criticized by American pre-Raphaelites who thought that "twenty times the study that the artist has given to this picture,-study represented by actual sketches, built upon a previous ten years ... would not have justified him in attempting to fill so large a canvas" (New Path, April 1864, 161, quoted in Anderson and Ferber 1990, 194). " <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://doi.org/10.2307%2F3179838">[4]</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Wingedserif" title="User:Wingedserif">Wingedserif</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Wingedserif" title="User talk:Wingedserif">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 16:41, 14 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li>Article new enough, created on May 7, the same day it was nominated. Long enough at over 4200 characters.</li> 
         <li>There are major problems with the references in this article; many don't support the statements made. For example, ref1 does say that Ruskin's book struck a chord with the Transcendalists, but p. 44 says nothing about plein air painting. Ref3 doesn't mention Emerson or Norton at all, and it doesn't mention Ruskin's painting. The last phrase in the last sentence of the fourth paragraph of the History section isn't supported by any source. Ref9 has the wrong page number; the article states that Richards became a marine painter on pp. 5 and 14. I'm sure you get my point, so I'll stop here. I'm unable to verify the sources in several refs because they're inaccessible, but I wouldn't be surprised if they suffered from the same issues. At any rate, this is a concerning issue with this article.</li> 
         <li>The first hook is fine, but there's nothing in the article about Bierstadt's painting.</li> 
         <li>There are major issues with the prose, which is secondary to the problems with the utilization of sources. The paragraphs are too short, probably because not enough information from the sources are included, giving this article a problem with comprehensiveness.</li> 
         <li>I can't pass this article in its current state. I recommend that you remove the nomination, give up the DYK, and work on how you use sources. <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_delete_vote.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol delete vote.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Symbol_delete_vote.svg/16px-Symbol_delete_vote.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Symbol_delete_vote.svg/24px-Symbol_delete_vote.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Symbol_delete_vote.svg/32px-Symbol_delete_vote.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <a href="/wiki/User:Figureskatingfan" title="User:Figureskatingfan">Christine (Figureskatingfan)</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Figureskatingfan" title="User talk:Figureskatingfan">talk</a>) 21:01, 31 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul> 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <dl>
           <dd>
            To your citation criticism: Ref1 was to connect Ruskin to Transcendental ideals, not plein air painting. Both the use of plein air painting and the popularity of <i>Modern Painters</i> are established by Ref3. Ref4 is to establish that Norton and Emerson in fact read <i>Modern Painters</i>. In Ref8 (I assume you meant), the relevant information is on the 12th page of the pdf—a mistake, yes, but a small one. As for the 4th graf of the history section, you'll notice that ref10 also establishes that the American Pre-Raphaelites criticized Bierstadt. The specific claim about the criticism of manifest destiny is verifiable in the Ferber 2019 source, which I have not had time to track down IRL. To me, none of this adds up to a "concerning issue" that fails to meet <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:V" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:V">WP:V</a> and can't be resolved w/ 1-2 edits. (As an aside, I wish you had phrased your criticism constructively instead of throwing your hands up.)
           </dd> 
           <dd>
            I do not believe the article's paragraphs are too short, and their length is not a result of "not enough information". I break paragraphs often because they help structure information for a reader. As far as I know, DYK does not have a comprehensiveness criteria, so I don't know why "a problem with comprehensiveness" is even part of the rationale for failing this nomination. At ~4200b, this article is well over the 1,500b requirement. —<u><i><a href="/wiki/User:Wingedserif" title="User:Wingedserif">Wingedserif</a></i></u> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Wingedserif" title="User talk:Wingedserif">talk</a>) 02:17, 1 June 2021 (UTC) 
            <dl>
             <dd>
              Having taken a quick look at this, I'm as baffled as <a href="/wiki/User:Wingedserif" title="User:Wingedserif">User:Wingedserif</a> as to why <a href="/wiki/User:Figureskatingfan" title="User:Figureskatingfan">User:Figureskatingfan</a> has reacted this harshly. I don't see "major issues with the prose"; what issues there are are minor enough to be addressed as part of this review. The paragraphs aren't unduly short and a "problem with comprehensiveness" would be relevant at Good Article Review but is odd grounds for denying a DYK. I urge the reviewer to give the author a chance to resolve the minor problems with the article. This could be a constructive and positive process, resulting in better quality articles, if we choose it to be. <a href="/wiki/User:MartinPoulter" title="User:MartinPoulter">MartinPoulter</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:MartinPoulter" title="User talk:MartinPoulter">talk</a>) 14:21, 1 June 2021 (UTC) 
              <dl>
               <dd>
                Sorry that I came across as harsh, I was trying to help make the article better. Yes, my comments about comprehensiveness are more general than what's needed more DYK, but I think that if the nominator followed my suggestions, it would improve it. I said that I couldn't pass it for DYK based upon the issues with the references and the utilization of sources; sorry if that wasn't made clear. I also was concerned that the same issues would appear in the sources that aren't accessible, which I suspect they do. My point is that your references need to support your statements and claims. I see that your statement about plein air painting is supported by ref3, but putting ref1 after the word "ideals," makes it look like the ref is supporting the entire phrase, including the claim about plein air painting. The solution, I think, is to put ref1 at the end of the sentence. Yes, this is being picky, but it was easy for me to assume that ref1 supports both claims when it doesn't, so the simple solution is to move the ref. I think that if an article lands on the main page, it needs to be accurate. If you fix the above issues, I'll assume that you fixed the issues about the inaccessible references and sources and will pass this for DYK. <a href="/wiki/User:Figureskatingfan" title="User:Figureskatingfan">Christine (Figureskatingfan)</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Figureskatingfan" title="User talk:Figureskatingfan">talk</a>) 17:09, 1 June 2021 (UTC)
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p>I see that you've resolved the above issues, so I'm passing this for DYK. Unrelated to this DYK: I think that this article has great potential for improvement, so I suggest that you work on it some more. I also suggest that you remove the "Legacy" section and put the one sentence in another place in the article, until you add more content about the American Pre-Raphaelites' affect on American art. That way, you can remove the tag. Thanks, best to you. <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_voting_keep.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol voting keep.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Symbol_voting_keep.svg/16px-Symbol_voting_keep.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Symbol_voting_keep.svg/24px-Symbol_voting_keep.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Symbol_voting_keep.svg/32px-Symbol_voting_keep.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <a href="/wiki/User:Figureskatingfan" title="User:Figureskatingfan">Christine (Figureskatingfan)</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Figureskatingfan" title="User talk:Figureskatingfan">talk</a>) 16:31, 2 June 2021 (UTC) </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Coster-Mullen">John Coster-Mullen</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJohn_Coster-Mullen&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/John_Coster-Mullen" title="John Coster-Mullen">John Coster-Mullen</a></b> discovered that the <a href="/wiki/Little_Boy" title="Little Boy">Little Boy</a> was actually a girl? <small>Source: "The atomic-research community was initially dubious about Coster-Mullen’s argument. But even Richard Rhodes, after examining the evidence, admitted that Coster-Mullen was right. Little Boy was female." (<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2008/12/15/atomic-john">[5]</a></small></li>

      <h4><span id="Karl-G.C3.BCnther_von_Hase"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Karl-Günther_von_Hase">Karl-Günther von Hase</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FKarl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 121px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase_thumb.jpg" class="image" title="Karl-Günther von Hase in 1964"><img alt="Karl-Günther von Hase in 1964" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase_thumb.jpg/121px-Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase_thumb.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="162" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase_thumb.jpg/182px-Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase_thumb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/40/Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase_thumb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="209" data-file-height="279"></a>

         Karl-Günther von Hase in 1964
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Karl-G%C3%BCnther_von_Hase" title="Karl-Günther von Hase">Karl-Günther von Hase</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, who had served as spokesman of the German government under three <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">chancellors</a>, became director of the <a href="/wiki/ZDF" title="ZDF">ZDF</a> broadcaster in 1977? <small>Source: several</small></li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Britain_Awake">Britain Awake</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBritain_Awake&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Britain_Awake&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 125px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg" class="image" title="Thatcher in 1975"><img alt="Thatcher in 1975" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg/125px-Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg/188px-Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg/250px-Margaret_Thatcher_in_September_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1191" data-file-height="1488"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Thatcher in 1975
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> <i>(pictured)</i> was first called the "Iron Lady" by a Soviet newspaper in response to <b><a href="/wiki/Britain_Awake" title="Britain Awake">a 1976 anti-communist speech</a></b>? <small>"‘Irony Lady’: How a Moscow propagandist gave Margaret Thatcher her famous nickname ... Krasnaya Zvezda, known as a mouthpiece for the Soviet army, was responding to a speech in which Thatcher had accused Moscow of seeking world domination ... The original Russian item carried the headline 'Zheleznaya Dama Ugrozhayet', which Evans translated as 'Iron Lady Wields Threats'"from: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFFisher2013" class="citation news cs1">Fisher, Max (8 April 2013). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2013/04/08/irony-lady-how-a-moscow-propagandist-gave-margaret-thatcher-her-famous-nickname/">"<span class="cs1-kern-left">'</span>Irony Lady': How a Moscow propagandist gave Margaret Thatcher her famous nickname"</a>. <i>Washington Post</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Washington+Post&amp;rft.atitle=%E2%80%98Irony+Lady%E2%80%99%3A+How+a+Moscow+propagandist+gave+Margaret+Thatcher+her+famous+nickname&amp;rft.date=2013-04-08&amp;rft.aulast=Fisher&amp;rft.aufirst=Max&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.washingtonpost.com%2Fnews%2Fworldviews%2Fwp%2F2013%2F04%2F08%2Firony-lady-how-a-moscow-propagandist-gave-margaret-thatcher-her-famous-nickname%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>'s 1976 <b><a href="/wiki/Britain_Awake" title="Britain Awake">"Britain Awake" speech</a></b> led to her being named the "Iron Lady" by a Soviet newspaper? <small>Source as ALT0</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_11"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_11">Articles created/expanded on May 11</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sather_Professorship_of_Classical_Literature">Sather Professorship of Classical Literature</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSather_Professorship_of_Classical_Literature&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sather_Professorship_of_Classical_Literature&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s> ... that until 1952 holders of the <b><a href="/wiki/Sather_Professorship_of_Classical_Literature" title="Sather Professorship of Classical Literature">Sather Professorship of Classical Literature</a></b> had access to a dedicated lavatory? </s><small>Source: Up to 1952 the Sather Professor had his own office in 470 Wheeler Hall, which was equipped with its own lavatory. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://escholarship.org/uc/item/5066c75h">Fontenrose</a> (1982) p. 18</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Valtellina_Redoubt" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Valtellina Redoubt">Template:Did you know nominations/Valtellina Redoubt</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Modussiccandi" title="User:Modussiccandi">Modussiccandi</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Modussiccandi" title="User talk:Modussiccandi">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 08:34, 12 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> Article creation date versus filing date okay. Article length meets the requirement. QPQ done.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li>But I don't like the hook at all. I'm all for off-beat attempts to draw reader attention, but this hook is trivial at best and diminishes the subject at worst.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li>I'm also concerned about the sourcing/neutrality of the article, in the sense that three of the four sources used are publications of Berkeley itself or its university press. Those sources can be used, but if this professorship is as important as the article makes it out to be, surely there are other outside sources that can be employed. In particular, an outside source might clarify if the professorship lectures themselves, and the books that come from them, have been influential in terms of their ideas and themes. Or rather is it that the professorship is prestigious because it is a reward for prior scholarly work. <a href="/wiki/User:Wasted_Time_R" title="User:Wasted Time R">Wasted Time R</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Wasted_Time_R" title="User talk:Wasted Time R">talk</a>) 01:55, 16 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul>

         <dd>
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Wasted_Time_R" title="User:Wasted Time R">Wasted Time R</a>:</span> I agree that the sourcing has too much UC Berkeley in it to be entirely neutral. I'll look out for more sources and ping you once that's done. Chances are a new hook will surface, too. Best, <a href="/wiki/User:Modussiccandi" title="User:Modussiccandi">Modussiccandi</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Modussiccandi" title="User talk:Modussiccandi">talk</a>) 09:04, 16 May 2021 (UTC)

Here is a suggestion for a new hook; let me know what you think. <a href="/wiki/User:Modussiccandi" title="User:Modussiccandi">Modussiccandi</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Modussiccandi" title="User talk:Modussiccandi">talk</a>) 13:58, 16 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

         <li><b>ALT1</b> ... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Sather_Professorship_of_Classical_Literature" title="Sather Professorship of Classical Literature">Sather Professorship of Classical Literature</a></b> was named after <a href="/wiki/Jane_K._Sather" class="mw-redirect" title="Jane K. Sather">Jane K. Sather</a> although her husband had accumulated the money to fund it? <small>Source: It was Peder and not Jane who had been the Trustee; and it was Peder who had accumulated most of the money. [...] But still, the name on the cornerstone of the tower is hers alone; the professorships are named for Jane, not for Peder. Dow (1965) 31.</small></li>

While the ALT1 hook is better than the original one, it seems a bit underwhelming. What about a hook that is based on the impact the Sather lectures/books have had? <a href="/wiki/User:Wasted_Time_R" title="User:Wasted Time R">Wasted Time R</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Wasted_Time_R" title="User talk:Wasted Time R">talk</a>) 21:43, 17 May 2021 (UTC)

              <ul>
               <li><b>ALT2</b> ... that <a href="/wiki/Helene_P._Foley" title="Helene P. Foley">Helene P. Foley</a>'s <b><a href="/wiki/Sather_Professorship_of_Classical_Literature" title="Sather Professorship of Classical Literature">Sather Lecture</a></b> on the <a href="/wiki/Classical_reception_studies" title="Classical reception studies">reception</a> of <a href="/wiki/Greek_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek theatre">Greek theatre</a> in the United States was described as "something of a milestone" in bringing the subject closer to the mainstream? <small>Source: Most have been published, and Reimagining Greek Tragedy on the American Stage, based on the lectures given by Helene Foley in 2007-08, is the seventieth volume in the series. It is remarkable - yet unremarked - that these were the first ever Sather Lectures to come under the broad umbrella of "Classical Reception". During the past twenty years or so the exploration of what has been made of and out of the classical cultures in modern times has moved from the margins into the mainstream. The incorporation of "Reception" under the Sather banner is, however, something of a milestone. And it is appropriate that this is devoted almost exclusively to American reception. Taplin (2013).</small></li>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_12"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_12">Articles created/expanded on May 12</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Embassy_of_the_Philippines.2C_Berlin"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Embassy_of_the_Philippines,_Berlin">Embassy of the Philippines, Berlin</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FEmbassy_of_the_Philippines%2C_Berlin&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Embassy_of_the_Philippines%2C_Berlin&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 157px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Philippinische_Botschaft,_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe,_2019-12-07_ama_fec_(3).jpg" class="image" title="The current chancery of the Philippine embassy in Berlin"><img alt="The current chancery of the Philippine embassy in Berlin" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Philippinische_Botschaft%2C_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe%2C_2019-12-07_ama_fec_%283%29.jpg/157px-Philippinische_Botschaft%2C_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe%2C_2019-12-07_ama_fec_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="157" height="125" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Philippinische_Botschaft%2C_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe%2C_2019-12-07_ama_fec_%283%29.jpg/236px-Philippinische_Botschaft%2C_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe%2C_2019-12-07_ama_fec_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Philippinische_Botschaft%2C_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe%2C_2019-12-07_ama_fec_%283%29.jpg/314px-Philippinische_Botschaft%2C_Luisenstra%C3%9Fe%2C_2019-12-07_ama_fec_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2277" data-file-height="1820"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         The current chancery of the Philippine embassy in Berlin
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_Philippines,_Berlin" title="Embassy of the Philippines, Berlin">Philippine embassy in Berlin</a></b> was once purportedly located above a supermarket, with <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_W%C3%BCrstchen" title="Frankfurter Würstchen">frankfurters</a> visible from the windows? <small>(Source: "Drilon said that he was given a tour of the chancery by then ambassador Jose Zaide and he could not forget the image of German frankfurters hanging outside the window. 'It’s an embarrassment. An embassy on top of a supermarket,' Drilon said." –<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.philstar.com/headlines/2012/08/15/838314/drilon-phl-chancery-wiener-view-embarrassing">The Philippine Star</a></i>)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the embassies of other Southeast Asian countries in Germany owned their buildings before the <b><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_Philippines,_Berlin" title="Embassy of the Philippines, Berlin">Philippine embassy in Berlin</a></b> did? <small>(Source: "Ambassador Delia Domingo-Albert has a dream. It is for the Philippine government to purchase the five-story building where Rizal once lived and convert it into a Chancery for the Philippine government. The Philippines is the only ASEAN embassy without a chancery and residence in Germany." –<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://news.abs-cbn.com/views-and-analysis/10/12/08/rizals-footsteps-leonor-magtolis-briones">ABS-CBN News</a>)</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="WSTJ">WSTJ</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWSTJ&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=WSTJ&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that Don Mullally, a DJ at Vermont radio station <b><a href="/wiki/WSTJ" title="WSTJ">WSTJ</a></b> between 1952 and 2016, left the air for good just two weeks before his death—still playing vinyl records? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.northlandjournal.com/don-mullally-a-northeast-kingdom-radio-legend/">[6]</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.vpr.org/post/craven-remembering-don-mullally#stream/0">[7]</a></small></li> 
       <li><b>ALT1</b> ... that Don Mullally, a DJ at Vermont radio station <b><a href="/wiki/WSTJ" title="WSTJ">WSTJ</a></b> between 1952 and 2016, was still playing vinyl records when he retired just two weeks before his death?</li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_13"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_13">Articles created/expanded on May 13</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 13">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stoney_Knoll_First_Nation">Stoney Knoll First Nation</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FStoney_Knoll_First_Nation&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stoney_Knoll_First_Nation&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Stoney_Knoll_First_Nation" title="Stoney Knoll First Nation">Stoney Knoll First Nation</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> <a href="/wiki/Indian_reserve" title="Indian reserve">Indian reserve</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Block_settlement#Mennonite" title="Block settlement">Mennonite reserve</a>? <small>Source: "This Mennonite Reserve as it was known was soon filled up, so that in October 1898, this land at Laird was added to it. So the former Young Chippewayan Indian Reserve now became a Reserve for Mennonite farmers." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://mcccanada.ca/sites/mcccanada.ca/files/media/saskatchewan/documents/young_chippewayan_indian_reserve.pdf">[8]</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <a href="/wiki/Mennonites" title="Mennonites">Mennonites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a> both think Canada should recognize the <b><a href="/wiki/Stoney_Knoll_First_Nation" title="Stoney Knoll First Nation">Stoney Knoll First Nation</a></b>? <small>Source: "Chief Weenie made it clear that the Young Chippewayan respected the current ownership of the land by the settlers and in turn Mennonite and Lutheran communities pledged support for the Young Chippewayan band’s ongoing struggle to obtain compensation for the land owed to them under Treaty Six after all these years." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://mcccanada.ca/sites/mcccanada.ca/files/media/saskatchewan/documents/young_chippewayan_indian_reserve.pdf">[9]</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: My third DYK. No QPQ requirement.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span id="Jack_Carson_.28cricketer.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jack_Carson_(cricketer)">Jack Carson (cricketer)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FJack_Carson_%28cricketer%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Jack_Carson_%28cricketer%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in his debut <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> season, <b><a href="/wiki/Jack_Carson_(cricketer)" title="Jack Carson (cricketer)">Jack Carson</a></b> took the most wickets of any <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County_Cricket_Club" title="Sussex County Cricket Club">Sussex</a> player in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Bob_Willis_Trophy" title="2020 Bob Willis Trophy">2020 Bob Willis Trophy</a>? <small>Source: Debut: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.espncricinfo.com/ci/engine/match/1227592.html">[10]</a>, Top wicket taker: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.cricketeurope.com/DATABASE/ARTICLES2020/articles/000012/001256.shtml">[11]</a></small></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Catherine_Sourbut_Groves">Catherine Sourbut Groves</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FCatherine_Sourbut_Groves&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Catherine_Sourbut_Groves" title="Catherine Sourbut Groves">Catherine Sourbut Groves</a></b> was made an archdeacon in the Church of England via Zoom? <small>Source: "You are strongly encouraged to quote the source text supporting each hook" (and [link] the source, or cite it briefly without using citation templates)</small>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hooded_visorbearer">Hooded visorbearer</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FHooded_visorbearer&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hooded_visorbearer&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 145px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_(cropped).jpg" class="image" title="Male hooded visorbearer"><img alt="Male hooded visorbearer" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_%28cropped%29.jpg/145px-Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="145" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_%28cropped%29.jpg/218px-Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_%28cropped%29.jpg/290px-Hooded_Visorbearer_Augastes_lumachella_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="636" data-file-height="593"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Male hooded visorbearer
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Hooded_visorbearer" title="Hooded visorbearer">hooded visorbearer</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> builds its <a href="/wiki/Bird_nest" title="Bird nest">nest</a> out of cactus spines? <small>Source: "It constructs nests out of cactus spikes in tree forks a metre from the ground" <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://datazone.birdlife.org/species/factsheet/hooded-visorbearer-augastes-lumachella/text">BirdLife International</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Hooded_visorbearer" title="Hooded visorbearer">hooded visorbearer</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> is <a href="/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature" title="Binomial nomenclature">scientifically named</a> <i>lumachella</i>, after the iridescent <a href="/wiki/Fire_marble" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire marble">fire marble</a>? <small>Source: "lumachella/lumachellus: Italian <i>lumachella</i>, fire marble, dark limestone containing shells which emit fiery reflections <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/Helm_Dictionary_of_Scientific_Bird_Names_by_James_A._Jobling/page/n231/mode/2up">The Helm Dictionary of Scientific Bird Names, p. 232</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Hooded_visorbearer" title="Hooded visorbearer">hooded visorbearer</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was thought to be extinct, until it was rediscovered in 1961? <small>Source: "a primeira espécie [<i>Augastes lumachellus</i>], dado como extinta (PINTO, 1938), foi redescoberta por Augusto Ruschi em 1961..." Translated = the first species [<i>Augastes lumachellus</i>], considered extinct (PINTO, 1938), was rediscovered by Augusto Ruschi in 1961... <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://periodicos.ufpb.br/index.php/revnebio/article/view/13820/9855">Aspectos da biologia e abundância do Beija-Flor-de-Gravatinha-Vermelha, <i>Augastes lumachellus</i> (Lesson, 1838) (Aves:Trochilidae), em Morro do Chapéu, BA (Translated = Aspects of biology and abundance of the hooded visorbearer, <i> Augastes lumachellus </i> (Lesson, 1838) (Aves: Trochilidae), in Morro do Chapéu, BA)</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Hooded_visorbearer" title="Hooded visorbearer">hooded visorbearer</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> may lose up to 90% of its range due to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>? <small>Source: "A projection of the impact of climate change on the species's range predicted that the area of the species's range would undergo a reduction of 80-90% by 2045-2060 (Marini et al. 2009)." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.iucnredlist.org/species/22688069/172881351#text-fields">IUCN Red List</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Hooded_visorbearer" title="Hooded visorbearer">hooded visorbearer</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> is found only in the <a href="/wiki/Chapada_Diamantina" title="Chapada Diamantina">Chapada Diamantina</a> mountains of <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">Bahia</a>, Brazil? <small>Source: "the previously cited <i>Augastes lumachellus</i> is endemic to the Chapada Diamantina replacing its co-generic from the south portion, <i>Augastes scutattus.</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.academia.edu/14747240">Towards greater knowledge of the Brazilian Semi-arid Biodiversity</a>, p. 102.</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Joel_Fagliano" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Joel Fagliano">Joel Fagliano</a></li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="19_East_54th_Street">19 East 54th Street</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2F19_East_54th_Street&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=19_East_54th_Street&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 124px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg" class="image" title="19 East 54th Street"><img alt="19 East 54th Street" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg/124px-Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg" decoding="async" width="124" height="157" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg/186px-Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg/248px-Minnie_E._Young_House_19_East_54th_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2190"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         19 East 54th Street
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that over the years, a converted house at <b><a href="/wiki/19_East_54th_Street" title="19 East 54th Street">19 East 54th Street</a></b> in New York City <i>(pictured)</i> has served as a dressmakers' showroom, antique gallery, salon, and bank office? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://s-media.nyc.gov/agencies/lpc/lp/2577.pdf">"Minnie E. Young House" (PDF). New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission. November 22, 2016.</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that when a firm at <b><a href="/wiki/19_East_54th_Street" title="19 East 54th Street">19 East 54th Street</a></b> went bankrupt, the company's lawyer partly blamed the "embarrassment of the company" on its relocation to the building? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://timesmachine.nytimes.com/timesmachine/1922/03/21/107049492.pdf">"Lucile's Creditors Force Receivership; Dressmakers Established by Lady Duff Gordon Owe $175,000, Have $75,000" (PDF). The New York Times. March 21, 1922. p. 10.</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that after hairdresser <a href="/wiki/Mr._Kenneth" title="Mr. Kenneth">Mr. Kenneth</a>'s salon in <b><a href="/wiki/19_East_54th_Street" title="19 East 54th Street">a converted New York City house</a></b> burned down, he lamented that "nothing like it will ever exist again"? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.vanityfair.com/news/2003/06/kenneth-battelle-hairdresser-jackie-kennedy">Collins, Amy Fine (May 14, 2003). "'Mr. Kenneth' Battelle: The Hairdresser Who Styled Jackie Kennedy, Marilyn Monroe, and Katharine Hepburn". Vanity Fair. </a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <p><b>Hook eligibility:</b> </p>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_14"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_14">Articles created/expanded on May 14</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 14">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_Defense_Communications_Satellite_Program">Initial Defense Communications Satellite Program</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FInitial_Defense_Communications_Satellite_Program&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Initial_Defense_Communications_Satellite_Program&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 157px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Idcspdep.jpg" class="image" title="Artist's rendering of a Transtage deploying IDSCP satellites"><img alt="Artist's rendering of a Transtage deploying IDSCP satellites" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Idcspdep.jpg/157px-Idcspdep.jpg" decoding="async" width="157" height="124" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Idcspdep.jpg/236px-Idcspdep.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Idcspdep.jpg/314px-Idcspdep.jpg 2x" data-file-width="693" data-file-height="548"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Artist's rendering of a Transtage deploying IDSCP satellites
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the photos transmitted from <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> by the <b><a href="/wiki/Initial_Defense_Communications_Satellite_Program" title="Initial Defense Communications Satellite Program">Initial Defense Communications Satellite Program</a></b> made possible near-real-time battlefield analysis during the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>? <small>Source: <sup id="cite_ref-beyondion_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beyondion-1">[1]</a></sup></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Initial_Defense_Communications_Satellite_Program" title="Initial Defense Communications Satellite Program">Initial Defense Communications Satellite Program</a></b>, launched 1966–1968, was the first operational United States military communications satellite constellation? <small>Source: <sup id="cite_ref-byrd_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byrd-2">[2]</a></sup></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Alfred_Tippinge" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Alfred Tippinge">Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Alfred_Tippinge</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Improved to Good Article status by <a href="/wiki/User:Neopeius" title="User:Neopeius">Neopeius</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Neopeius" title="User talk:Neopeius">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 03:03, 15 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a>Article has been improved to GA status (laudable considering its very new as well). Long enough and meets prose policy guidelines. Hook meets guidelines as well and ALT0 is very interesting. QPQ done and image is in the public domain in the United States and therefore meets copyright stipulations. <a href="/wiki/User:Jupitus_Smart" title="User:Jupitus Smart"><b><span style="color:#f45342;">Jupitus</span> <span style="color:#05ad83"><i>Smart</i></span></b></a> 18:15, 28 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul>

      <h4><span id="Max_Liebling.2C_Georg_Liebling"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Max_Liebling,_Georg_Liebling">Max Liebling, Georg Liebling</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMax_Liebling&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Max_Liebling&amp;action=history">Max Liebling</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Max_Liebling" title="Max Liebling">Max Liebling</a></b> and his three brothers, <b><a href="/wiki/Georg_Liebling" title="Georg Liebling">Georg</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Emil_Liebling" title="Emil Liebling">Emil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sally_Liebling" title="Sally Liebling">Sally Liebling</a>, were all successful concert pianists and composers who trained under <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a>? <small>Source: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFCharlotte_Greenspan2009" class="citation web cs1">Charlotte Greenspan (2009). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://jwa.org/encyclopedia/article/liebling-estelle">"Estelle Liebling: 1880 – 1970"</a>. <i>The Encyclopedia of Jewish Women</i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Encyclopedia+of+Jewish+Women&amp;rft.atitle=Estelle+Liebling%3A+1880+%E2%80%93+1970&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.au=Charlotte+Greenspan&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fjwa.org%2Fencyclopedia%2Farticle%2Fliebling-estelle&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span>)</small></li>

The article passes DYK requirements, and it's a worthwhile subject - thank you for uploading it. The following comments do not affect the DYK status: It would improve the article a great deal if the main text were shaped a little more, though, because at the moment that section is a wall of text. I suggest separating out paragraphs 1, 4 and 5 of the main text, and calling it "Life", "Private life" or similar, and then calling paras 2 and 3 "Career" after that. Also, is <a href="/wiki/Max_Liebling_House" title="Max Liebling House">Max Liebling House</a> named after him? If so, it would be nice to include that information at the end of the article, perhaps under another subheading and with a picture of the house. <a href="/wiki/User:Storye_book" title="User:Storye book">Storye book</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Storye_book" title="User talk:Storye book">talk</a>) 09:56, 22 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Red-billed_pied_tanager">Red-billed pied tanager</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRed-billed_pied_tanager&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Red-billed_pied_tanager&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 191px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg" class="image" title="Red-billed pied tanager"><img alt="Red-billed pied tanager" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg/191px-Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg" decoding="async" width="191" height="102" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg/287px-Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg/382px-Lamprospiza_melanoleuca-20090124.jpg 2x" data-file-width="766" data-file-height="410"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Red-billed pied tanager
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Red-billed_pied_tanager" title="Red-billed pied tanager">red-billed pied tanager</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> is not a <a href="/wiki/Tanager" title="Tanager">tanager</a>? <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.researchgate.net/publication/233891607_Going_to_Extremes_Contrasting_Rates_of_Diversification_in_a_Recent_Radiation_of_New_World_Passerine_Birds">Source</a> - at the end of the paper, species moved out of tanager family into new family.</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Ronald_Graham_(actor)" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Ronald Graham (actor)">Template:Did you know nominations/Ronald Graham (actor)</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>
