      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Electoral_history_of_John_Quincy_Adams">Electoral history of John Quincy Adams</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FElectoral_history_of_John_Quincy_Adams&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electoral_history_of_John_Quincy_Adams&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 126px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:JQA_Photo.tif_(cropped).jpg" class="image" title="John Quincy Adams in early 1840's"><img alt="John Quincy Adams in early 1840's" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JQA_Photo.tif_%28cropped%29.jpg/126px-JQA_Photo.tif_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="126" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JQA_Photo.tif_%28cropped%29.jpg/189px-JQA_Photo.tif_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/JQA_Photo.tif_%28cropped%29.jpg/252px-JQA_Photo.tif_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="915" data-file-height="1126"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams" title="John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a> in early 1840's
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Electoral_history_of_John_Quincy_Adams" title="Electoral history of John Quincy Adams">John Quincy Adams</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was the only <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">American president</a> to be elected as a member of <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> after leaving the presidency? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://history.house.gov/Historical-Highlights/1800-1850/The-election-of-John-Quincy-Adams-of-Massachusetts/">History, Art &amp; Archives</a>; <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.americaslibrary.gov/aa/jqadams/aa_jqadams_congressma_1.html#:~:text=John%20Quincy%20Adams%20as%20a%20Congressman&amp;text=After%20losing%20the%201828%20election,the%20U.S.%20House%20of%20Representatives.">America's Library</a> "The November 1, 1830, election made Adams the first and only former President to be elected to the House of Representatives."</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Simonie_Michael" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Simonie Michael">Simonie Michael</a></li>

Shanbhag</a></b> started <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>'s landmark Premier Bookstore at the site of a burned down clothing store in 1971? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.economist.com/obituary/2021/05/15/ts-shanbhag-died-of-coronavirus-on-may-4th">https://www.economist.com/obituary/2021/05/15/ts-shanbhag-died-of-coronavirus-on-may-4th</a></small></li>

      <h4><span id="Embassy_of_the_Philippines.2C_The_Hague"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Embassy_of_the_Philippines,_The_Hague">Embassy of the Philippines, The Hague</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FEmbassy_of_the_Philippines%2C_The_Hague&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Embassy_of_the_Philippines%2C_The_Hague&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg" class="image" title="Chancery of the Philippine embassy in The Hague"><img alt="Chancery of the Philippine embassy in The Hague" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg/162px-L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg/243px-L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg/324px-L%27Haia_ambaixada_filipina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="972"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Chancery of the Philippine embassy in The Hague
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the Philippines' <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Philippines)" title="Department of Foreign Affairs (Philippines)">Department of Foreign Affairs</a> says it won't arrest communist leader <a href="/wiki/Jose_Maria_Sison" title="Jose Maria Sison">Jose Maria Sison</a> if he vists the <b><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_the_Philippines,_The_Hague" title="Embassy of the Philippines, The Hague">Philippine embassy in The Hague</a></b>? <small>(Source: "'No, I will not enforce that warrant of arrest in that embassy abroad," Locsin told members of the Commission on Appointments (CA) when asked [...] 'If I were to enforce that and arrest him, [...] we would present an international spectacle that would invite laughter first and then outrage,' he said." –<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://news.abs-cbn.com/news/12/09/20/arrest-warrant-vs-joma-sison-wont-be-enforced-inside-ph-embassies-locsin">ABS-CBN News and Current Affairs</a>)</small></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Romani_people_in_Poland">Romani people in Poland</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRomani_people_in_Poland&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Romani_people_in_Poland&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Romani_people_in_Poland" title="Romani people in Poland">Roma people</a></b> were persecuted alongside the Jews in the Holocaust? <small>Source: "The motives invoked to justify the death of the Gypsies were the same as those ordering the murder of the Jews, and the methods employed for the one were identical with those employed for the other." (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1057/9780230524507_18#citeas">https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1057/9780230524507_18#citeas</a>)</small></li>
      </ul>

      <p><b>Overall</b>: <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <s>This expansion doesn't seem sufficient to meet the criteria of five-fold expansion: 00:28, 12 May 2021 (6199 characters, 943 words), 18:56, 17 May 2021? (18332 characters, 2787 words). There was no significant expansion in the seven day interval prior to nomination. I'd be happy to find out I was incorrect.</s> <a href="/wiki/User:BusterD" title="User:BusterD">BusterD</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:BusterD" title="User talk:BusterD">talk</a>) 08:07, 3 June 2021 (UTC) </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><b>Comment</b>. At the suggestion of a more experienced DYK reviewer I was wondering if there would be any objection to including expansion by <a href="/wiki/User:Coreou" title="User:Coreou">User:Coreou</a> in the total. Both of these editors are students studying Wikipedia (at different schools on opposite sides of the world, if I read correctly) and together their work easily surpasses the length requirement, taking the article from <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Romani_people_in_Poland&amp;oldid=1019590095">this</a> to the much better <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Romani_people_in_Poland&amp;oldid=1024926368">this</a>. Excellent work for new wikipedians. The new numbers would be 06:46, 24 April 2021? (242 words, 1559 characters), 17 May 2021? (2787 words, 18332 characters) a 11x expansion. Technically this is actually 23 days of work instead of 7, but with both editors being enthusatic new students, I'm wondering if this could be allowed for. The downside is that both editors would take credit for the expansion, but I see that as a positive, not a negative. Issues? Agreement? <a href="/wiki/User:BusterD" title="User:BusterD">BusterD</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:BusterD" title="User talk:BusterD">talk</a>) 21:15, 3 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul> 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <ul>
           <li><b>Comment</b>. Both of these student editors contribute very occasionally. <a href="/wiki/User:Coreou" title="User:Coreou">User:Coreou</a> last edited on 1 May, <a href="/wiki/User:RimaB99" title="User:RimaB99">User:RimaB99</a> last editing on 1 June. I'm going to give this MY approval, based on my comment above. If I'm wrong in stretching the time frame in order to include both editors (one in Tennessee, one in Australia) in 11x expansion, then I'll cop to it. I think this is a great Wikipedia story, and I want to endorse such world-wide collaboration by student editors. BTW, QPQ not required for these new contributors. <a href="/wiki/User:BusterD" title="User:BusterD">BusterD</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:BusterD" title="User talk:BusterD">talk</a>) 05:46, 5 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
          </ul>
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lisl_Goldarbeiter">Lisl Goldarbeiter</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FLisl_Goldarbeiter&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lisl_Goldarbeiter&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 121px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Miss_Austria_1929_(Lisl_Goldarbeiter),_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg" class="image" title="Portrait of Lisl Goldarbeiter (1929)"><img alt="Portrait of Lisl Goldarbeiter (1929)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Miss_Austria_1929_%28Lisl_Goldarbeiter%29%2C_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg/121px-Miss_Austria_1929_%28Lisl_Goldarbeiter%29%2C_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Miss_Austria_1929_%28Lisl_Goldarbeiter%29%2C_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg/182px-Miss_Austria_1929_%28Lisl_Goldarbeiter%29%2C_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Miss_Austria_1929_%28Lisl_Goldarbeiter%29%2C_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg/242px-Miss_Austria_1929_%28Lisl_Goldarbeiter%29%2C_by_Hermann_Schieberth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="637" data-file-height="850"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Portrait of Lisl Goldarbeiter (1929)
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in 1929, <b><a href="/wiki/Lisl_Goldarbeiter" title="Lisl Goldarbeiter">Lisl Goldarbeiter</a></b> became the first Austrian to win the <a href="/wiki/International_Pageant_of_Pulchritude" title="International Pageant of Pulchritude">Miss Universe</a> title? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.moderntimes.review/first-austrian-miss-universe-1929/">The first and only Austrian Miss Universe 1929</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://jfi.org/watch-online/jfi-on-demand/miss-universe-1929-lisl-goldarbeiter-a-queen-in-wien">Lisl Goldarbeiter was ... living in Vienna in the 1920s who eventually was crowned Austria’s first—and only—Miss Universe</a> </small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Lisl_Goldarbeiter" title="Lisl Goldarbeiter">Lisl Goldarbeiter</a></b> was the first non-American to win the title of <a href="/wiki/International_Pageant_of_Pulchritude" title="International Pageant of Pulchritude">Miss Universe</a>? <small>Source:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.moderntimes.review/first-austrian-miss-universe-1929/">The first and only Austrian Miss Universe 1929</a> </small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that when Austrian <b><a href="/wiki/Lisl_Goldarbeiter" title="Lisl Goldarbeiter">Lisl Goldarbeiter</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> won the 1929 <a href="/wiki/International_Pageant_of_Pulchritude" title="International Pageant of Pulchritude">Miss Universe</a> contest, the 2nd, 3rd, 4th and 5th places were all taken by Americans? <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090808153929/http://www.pageantopolis.com/international/universe_1920.htm">Source here</a> by <a href="/wiki/User:Victuallers" title="User:Victuallers">Victuallers</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Victuallers" title="User talk:Victuallers">talk</a>) 13:52, 20 May 2021 (UTC)</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Amna_Suraka">Amna Suraka</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FAmna_Suraka&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amna_Suraka&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;">

      </dl> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fanny_Howie">Fanny Howie</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FFanny_Howie&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fanny_Howie&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 134px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie,_about_1898_01_(cropped).jpg" class="image" title="Fanny Howie, circa 1898"><img alt="Fanny Howie, circa 1898" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie%2C_about_1898_01_%28cropped%29.jpg/134px-Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie%2C_about_1898_01_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="134" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie%2C_about_1898_01_%28cropped%29.jpg/201px-Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie%2C_about_1898_01_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie%2C_about_1898_01_%28cropped%29.jpg/268px-Signed_photograph_of_Fanny_Rose_Howie%2C_about_1898_01_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="345"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Fanny Howie, circa 1898
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that New Zealand singer <b><a href="/wiki/Fanny_Howie" title="Fanny Howie">Fanny Howie</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> composed the song "<a href="/wiki/Hine_e_Hine" class="mw-redirect" title="Hine e Hine">Hine e Hine</a>", which aired on New Zealand television every night from 1981 to 1994?<small> Source: "The ‘Goodnight Kiwi’, by animator Sam Harvey, appeared nightly to signal the end of transmission on Television New Zealand between 1981 and 1994. (...) The instantly recognisable tune is 'Hine e hine', a lullaby written by Fanny Rose Howie." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://teara.govt.nz/en/video/10197/goodnight-kiwi">[13]</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that New Zealand singer <b><a href="/wiki/Fanny_Howie" title="Fanny Howie">Fanny Howie</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> performed under the stage name Te Rangi Pai, which was a shortened version of her mother's name meaning "the beautiful sky"? <small>Source: "By 1900 she was using as a stage name a shortened version of her mother's name, Te Rangi Pai, which means 'the beautiful sky'." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://teara.govt.nz/en/biographies/3h40/howie-fanny-rose">[14]</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: No QPQ required, as this is my fourth nomination.</li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Many thanks, and I'm open to any suggestions for improvement.</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_of_Ladakh">Culture of Ladakh</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FCulture_of_Ladakh&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Culture_of_Ladakh&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ladakh" title="Culture of Ladakh">culture of Ladakh</a></b> has several festivals throughout the year, with the most famous ones being <a href="/wiki/Hemis_Monastery#Hemis_Festival" title="Hemis Monastery">Hemis Tsechu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Losar" title="Losar">Losar</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.jagranjosh.com/current-affairs/losar-the-biggest-tibetan-buddhist-festival-began-in-ladakh-region-1450084394-1">[15]</a> Losar, the biggest Tibetan Buddhist Festival, began in Ladakh region</small> <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.latimes.com/travel/la-tr-fulleventjan22-story.html">[16]</a> Major festivals, events around the world</small></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebecca_Dayan">Rebecca Dayan</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRebecca_Dayan&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rebecca_Dayan&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that actress <b><a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Dayan" title="Rebecca Dayan">Rebecca Dayan</a></b> developed a love for acting while being raised in a hotel? <small>Source: "Dayan developed a devotion to acting and art as a child growing up first in the hotel her parents owned" <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.wmagazine.com/story/rebecca-dayan-novitiate-style-david-bowie">[17]</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Dayan" title="Rebecca Dayan">Rebecca Dayan</a></b> was trained as an artist, then tried out acting, then exhibited art, then got major acting roles? <small>Source: "Dayan’s interest in painting is a homecoming, in a way. It’s what she originally studied in Nice [...] In 2009 she took a leap of faith over the Atlantic Ocean to New York, eventually breaking into acting [...] it was during her sojourn in the movies that she returned to art." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://wwd.com/fashion-news/designer-luxury/model-actress-rebecca-dayan-painting-10203205/">[18]</a> (2015) and "Her first major role [...] may propel her into the spotlight, but her work off-screen deserves just as much attention. Dayan, who was raised in the South of France and studied art and fashion design in Paris, has always tapped into her expansive artistic expressions." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://coveteur.com/2017/10/24/rebecca-dayan-novitiate-actress-french-girl-obsession/">[19]</a> (2017) ...</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that working on the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Novitiate_(film)" title="Novitiate (film)">Novitiate</a></i>, in which she plays a nun, inspired actress and artist <b><a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Dayan" title="Rebecca Dayan">Rebecca Dayan</a></b> to create religious virgin art for her 2015 collection "Assumption"? <small>Source: "I had been in talks with Maggie about [Novitiate] for a long time, and she had sent me all these books that I was deep into reading. When I got asked to do this art show, I couldn’t possibly think of anything else. I got drawn to ideas of sexuality and religion. I read pieces of writing about virgins and what that meant before Christianity." [ditto]</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Dayan" title="Rebecca Dayan">Rebecca Dayan</a></b>, who portrays model and designer <a href="/wiki/Elsa_Peretti" title="Elsa Peretti">Elsa Peretti</a> in miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Halston_(miniseries)" title="Halston (miniseries)">Halston</a></i>, was also a model and designer before she took up acting? <small>Source: "Peretti [...] The Italian-born model turned jewelry designer [and] the woman who plays her in Halston: French actor Rebecca Dayan [...] [Dayan] went into fashion design and modeling in Paris" <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.glamour.com/story/rebecca-dayan-halston">[20]</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that actress <b><a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Dayan" title="Rebecca Dayan">Rebecca Dayan</a></b> has produced a documentary about, and started a non-profit to advocate in relation to, <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality_in_the_United_States" title="Maternal mortality in the United States">maternal mortality in the United States</a>? <small>Source: "Beyond acting, [Dayan has] co-founded the non-profit Mother Lover, which seeks to raise awareness of the maternal health crisis in the US, and produced the documentary Born Free on the same topic." <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.vogue.co.uk/arts-and-lifestyle/article/rebecca-dayan-halston-interview">[21]</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 120px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_(cropped).jpg" class="image" title="Riyoko Ikeda"><img alt="Riyoko Ikeda" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_%28cropped%29.jpg/120px-2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="162" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-2008TIBE_Hall2_ComicPavilion_Opening_RiyokoIkeda_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="941" data-file-height="1272"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Riyoko Ikeda
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Riyoko_Ikeda" title="Riyoko Ikeda">Riyoko Ikeda</a> <i>(pictured)</i> wrote her manga series <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Rose_of_Versailles" title="The Rose of Versailles">The Rose of Versailles</a></b></i> as a story about revolution and populist uprising after becoming involved with the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Communist_Party" title="Japanese Communist Party">Japanese Communist Party</a> in the 1960s? <small>Source: "<i>The Rose of Versailles</i>: Women and Revolution in Girls' Manga and the Socialist Movement in Japan"</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the sole copy of an English-language translation of the manga series <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Rose_of_Versailles" title="The Rose of Versailles">The Rose of Versailles</a></b></i> produced in the 1970s was lost? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.animenewsnetwork.com/jason-thompson-house-of-1000-manga/the-rose-of-versailles/2010-05-06">Anime News Network</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that Japanese manga artist <a href="/wiki/Riyoko_Ikeda" title="Riyoko Ikeda">Riyoko Ikeda</a> <i>(pictured)</i> was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a> by the French government for her manga series <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Rose_of_Versailles" title="The Rose of Versailles">The Rose of Versailles</a></b></i>? <small>Source: "<i>La Rose de Versailles</i>: Marie-Antoinette, une reine martyre mangaïsée"</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span id="National_Museum_of_Ireland_.E2.80.93_Decorative_Arts_and_History"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Museum_of_Ireland_–_Decorative_Arts_and_History">National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FNational_Museum_of_Ireland_%E2%80%93_Decorative_Arts_and_History&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=National_Museum_of_Ireland_%E2%80%93_Decorative_Arts_and_History&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 121px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Collins%27_slippers_(NMI).jpg" class="image" title="The viral blue wolf slippers"><img alt="The viral blue wolf slippers" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Michael_Collins%27_slippers_%28NMI%29.jpg/121px-Michael_Collins%27_slippers_%28NMI%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Michael_Collins%27_slippers_%28NMI%29.jpg/182px-Michael_Collins%27_slippers_%28NMI%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Michael_Collins%27_slippers_%28NMI%29.jpg/242px-Michael_Collins%27_slippers_%28NMI%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         The viral blue wolf slippers
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that a major Asian collection was donated to the <b><a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Ireland_%E2%80%93_Decorative_Arts_and_History" title="National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History">National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History</a></b> by Jewish benefactor <a href="/wiki/Albert_M._Bender" title="Albert M. Bender">Albert Bender</a> while the museum was headed by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Mahr" title="Adolf Mahr">Adolf Mahr</a>, head of the Dublin <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> chapter? <small>Source: Letters from our 'No. One Nazi'". <i>The Irish Times</i>. 19 September 2000.</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that a pair of blue slippers with a wolf's head pattern, held by the <b><a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Ireland_%E2%80%93_Decorative_Arts_and_History" title="National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History">National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History</a></b>, which belonged to Irish revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Michael_Collins_(Irish_leader)" title="Michael Collins (Irish leader)">Michael Collins</a>, went viral online in 2021? <small>Source: "Michael Collins' wolf slippers spark Twitter storm". <i>BBC News</i>. 27 February 2021</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that the exhibition <i>The Way We Wore</i> at the <b><a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Ireland_%E2%80%93_Decorative_Arts_and_History" title="National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History">National Museum of Ireland – Decorative Arts and History</a></b> displays Irish clothing from a span of 250 years, including work by <a href="/wiki/Sybil_Connolly" title="Sybil Connolly">Sybil Connolly</a>? <small>Source: The Way We Wore". The Costume Society</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span id="Heiligen-Geist-Kapelle.2C_Bruck"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Heiligen-Geist-Kapelle,_Bruck">Heiligen-Geist-Kapelle, Bruck</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FHeiligen-Geist-Kapelle%2C_Bruck&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Heiligen-Geist-Kapelle%2C_Bruck&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul>

       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Bruck_L1400826.jpg" class="image" title="Vault in the chapel"><img alt="Vault in the chapel" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bruck_L1400826.jpg/162px-Bruck_L1400826.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="121" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bruck_L1400826.jpg/243px-Bruck_L1400826.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bruck_L1400826.jpg/324px-Bruck_L1400826.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2835" data-file-height="2126"></a>

         Vault in the chapel

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gourd_mouth_organ">Gourd mouth organ</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FGourd_mouth_organ&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gourd_mouth_organ&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 115px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg" class="image" title="Art from Tang dynasty showing a musician playing the mouth organ (2nd left)"><img alt="Art from Tang dynasty showing a musician playing the mouth organ (2nd left)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg/115px-Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg" decoding="async" width="115" height="171" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg/173px-Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg/230px-Traditional_Chinese_instrument_players_-_Yulin_Cave_25.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="774"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Art from Tang dynasty showing a musician playing the mouth organ (2nd left)
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Gourd_mouth_organ" title="Gourd mouth organ">Gourd mouth organ</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was invented 3000 years ago? Source: <small>Sachs, C. (2012). The history of musical instruments. Courier Corporation. ISBN 0486171515</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <p><s>** <b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Gourd_mouth_organ" title="Gourd mouth organ">Gourd mouth organ</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> is believed to be invented by Chinese goddess Nüwa?</s> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that the tallest <b><a href="/wiki/Gourd_mouth_organ" title="Gourd mouth organ">Gourd mouth organ</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> can go up to about 12 feet? Source: <small>Chapman, A. (2005). Breath and bamboo: Diasporic Lao identity and the Lao mouth-organ. Journal of Intercultural Studies, 26(1-2), 5-20.</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_19"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_19">Articles created/expanded on May 19</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 19">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span id="Lisa_H.C3.B6pink"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lisa_Höpink">Lisa Höpink</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FLisa_H%C3%B6pink&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lisa_H%C3%B6pink&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that German swimmer <b><a href="/wiki/Lisa_H%C3%B6pink" title="Lisa Höpink">Lisa Höpink</a></b>, who was twice named Germany's young swimmer of the year, won two medals at the <a href="/wiki/2019_Summer_Universiade" title="2019 Summer Universiade">2019 Summer Universiade</a>?</s> <small>Source: Swimmer of the Year: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.swimpool.de/schwimmen/kader-talente/schwimmer-und-jugendschwimmer-des-jahres/jugendschwimmer-des-jahres.html">[22]</a> ("Jugendschwimmer(in) des Jahres" translates as youth/young swimmer of the year), Medals: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://swimsportnews.de/9605-lisa-hoepink-holt-zweite-universiade-medaille">[23]</a> " Lisa Höpink holt zweite Universiade-Medaille" ("Lisa Höpink wins second Universiade medal") &amp; <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://swimsportnews.de/9599-silber-in-italien-lisa-hoepink-wird-zweite-bei-der-universiade-2019">[24]</a> explicitly mentions 1st medal</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Sing_(Travis_song)" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Sing (Travis song)">Template:Did you know nominations/Sing (Travis song)</a></li>
        </ul>

       <li>Free of <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Copyright_violations" title="Wikipedia:Copyright violations">copyright violations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Plagiarism" title="Wikipedia:Plagiarism">plagiarism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Close_paraphrasing" title="Wikipedia:Close paraphrasing">close paraphrasing</a>: <img alt="Question" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Blue_question_mark_%28italic%29.svg/20px-Blue_question_mark_%28italic%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Blue_question_mark_%28italic%29.svg/30px-Blue_question_mark_%28italic%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Blue_question_mark_%28italic%29.svg/40px-Blue_question_mark_%28italic%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600"><span style="display:none">?</span></li>
      </ul>

      <p><b>Overall</b>: <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_question.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol question.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/16px-Symbol_question.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/24px-Symbol_question.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Symbol_question.svg/32px-Symbol_question.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> The hook and the article mention that she was named Germany's young swimmer of the year. Who awarded this honour, and are they a reputable organisation? Unfortunately, I do not speak German so I was not able to determine this from the source. Please ping me once this is specified in the article and I will review if the information needs to be added to the hook. <a href="/wiki/User:Z1720" title="User:Z1720">Z1720</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Z1720" title="User talk:Z1720">talk</a>) 14:51, 5 June 2021 (UTC) </p>

         <dd>
          Thanks for checking, I spotted a mistake in the hook, as the award was not for national swimmer of the year, just state swimmer of the year (as it was awarded by the <a href="/wiki/NRW" class="mw-redirect" title="NRW">NRW</a> state swimming association). How about:
         </dd> 
         <dd>
          <b>ALT1</b>: ... that German swimmer <b><a href="/wiki/Lisa_H%C3%B6pink" title="Lisa Höpink">Lisa Höpink</a></b>, who has qualified for two events at the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a>, won two medals at the <a href="/wiki/2019_Summer_Universiade" title="2019 Summer Universiade">2019 Summer Universiade</a>?
         </dd> 
         <dd>
          Source for Universaide medals are as above, for Olympics there is <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.swimmingworldmagazine.com/news/florian-wellbrock-swims-344-400-free-on-night-two-of-germanys-olympic-qualifier/">[25]</a> "Germany qualified a women's and men's 4×100 free relay for Tokyo as Annika Bruhn led the 100 free field on the women’s side at 53.96 ahead of Lisa Hopink (54.65) and Marie Pietruschka (54.73) while Hannah Kuchler was fourth at 54.88." (for 4 x 100 relay qualified), and for 4 x 100 medley source, it would be <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://swim.de/aktuell/lisa-hoepink-und-ole-braunschweig-zum-ersten-mal-bei-olympia-dabei/">[26]</a> (translation of the first sentence of the "Höpink und Kusch schmettern am schnellsten" section is "Lisa Höpink secured a place in the mixed relay over 4 x 100 metres on 100 metres butterfly"). <a href="/wiki/User:Joseph2302" title="User:Joseph2302"><b style="color:#0033ab">Joseph</b></a><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Joseph2302" title="User talk:Joseph2302"><b style="color:#000000">2302</b></a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Joseph2302" title="User talk:Joseph2302">talk</a>) 16:39, 5 June 2021 (UTC) 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            I would suggest putting the information in chronological order, as so:
           </dd> 
           <dd>
            <b>ALT2</b>: ... that German swimmer <b><a href="/wiki/Lisa_H%C3%B6pink" title="Lisa Höpink">Lisa Höpink</a></b> won two medals at the <a href="/wiki/2019_Summer_Universiade" title="2019 Summer Universiade">2019 Summer Universiade</a> and qualified for two events at the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a>?

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Five_Brahms_Waltzes_in_the_Manner_of_Isadora_Duncan">Five Brahms Waltzes in the Manner of Isadora Duncan</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FFive_Brahms_Waltzes_in_the_Manner_of_Isadora_Duncan&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Five_Brahms_Waltzes_in_the_Manner_of_Isadora_Duncan&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Ashton" title="Frederick Ashton">Frederick Ashton</a>'s ballet <i><b><a href="/wiki/Five_Brahms_Waltzes_in_the_Manner_of_Isadora_Duncan" title="Five Brahms Waltzes in the Manner of Isadora Duncan">Five Brahms Waltzes in the Manner of Isadora Duncan</a></b></i> took inspiration from a performance by <a href="/wiki/Isadora_Duncan" title="Isadora Duncan">Isadora Duncan</a> he saw when he was 17? <small>Source: "When Frederick Ashton choreographed Five Brahms Waltzes in the Manner of Isadora Duncan, he was drawing on his own 55-year-old memories of the great dancer. Back in 1921 he was a ballet-obsessed 17-year-old while Duncan, aged 44, was well past her prime." (<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.theguardian.com/stage/2004/feb/21/dance.art">[27]</a>)</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Wo_Menschen_sich_vergessen" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Wo Menschen sich vergessen">Wo Menschen sich vergessen</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Corachow" title="User:Corachow">Corachow</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Corachow" title="User talk:Corachow">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 10:51, 19 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Would like to review, but later. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 15:25, 1 June 2021 (UTC)
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> Interesting ballet and story, on fine sources, no copyvio opbvious. In the hook, I believe mentioning the flying petals would be extra hooky. In the article, I am no friend of the wording "her petal dance to", and I count to 6 numbers for waltzes. --<a href="/wiki/User:Gerda_Arendt" title="User:Gerda Arendt">Gerda Arendt</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Gerda_Arendt" title="User talk:Gerda Arendt">talk</a>) 20:33, 1 June 2021 (UTC) 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          Thanks for the review. I corrected the problems. According to a dance company's website, Waltz No. 1 is used as a prelude before the dancer enters, somehow I forgot to put that in the article. <a href="/wiki/User:Corachow" title="User:Corachow">Corachow</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Corachow" title="User talk:Corachow">talk</a>) 21:06, 1 June 2021 (UTC)
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>

      <h4><span id="Saint_John.27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_.28Kingman.2C_Arizona.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_John's_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_(Kingman,_Arizona)">Saint John's Methodist Episcopal Church (Kingman, Arizona)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSaint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_%28Kingman%2C_Arizona%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_%28Kingman%2C_Arizona%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 188px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman,_Arizona_(cropped).JPG" class="image" title="Saint John's Methodist Episcopal Church"><img alt="Saint John's Methodist Episcopal Church" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman%2C_Arizona_%28cropped%29.JPG/188px-Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman%2C_Arizona_%28cropped%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="188" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman%2C_Arizona_%28cropped%29.JPG/282px-Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman%2C_Arizona_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman%2C_Arizona_%28cropped%29.JPG/376px-Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_Kingman%2C_Arizona_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2217" data-file-height="1236"></a>

      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Clark_Gable" title="Clark Gable">Clark Gable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carole_Lombard" title="Carole Lombard">Carole Lombard</a> were married at <b><a href="/wiki/Saint_John%27s_Methodist_Episcopal_Church_(Kingman,_Arizona)" title="Saint John's Methodist Episcopal Church (Kingman, Arizona)">Saint John's Methodist Episcopal Church</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> after eloping in 1939? <small>Source: ref 3 says "the pair eloped in Kingman, Arizona." ref 4 is one of many sources that say it was at this church.</small></li>

      </table> 
      <p><b>Overall</b>: <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> All good. Photo credit checks out, the article's in good shape, the sources verify that Gable and Lombard did indeed get married at the church, and it's certainly interesting enough – I'd expect a few page hits for this one. I really have no option other than to pass, so congrats! <a href="/wiki/User:AllegedlyHuman" title="User:AllegedlyHuman">AllegedlyHuman</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:AllegedlyHuman" title="User talk:AllegedlyHuman">talk</a>) 08:57, 25 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wild_Bird_Fund">Wild Bird Fund</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FWild_Bird_Fund&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wild_Bird_Fund&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Wild_Bird_Fund" title="Wild Bird Fund">Wild Bird Fund</a></b> is <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s first and only wildlife hospital?</li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>

         <li><i>Comment</i>: <s>I'm working on securing an image for this. Please hold off a couple days before promoting?</s> <i>Update:</i> Good to go. Got some photos. All otrs pending at the moment, though. Adding a couple options that would look good on the main page here. I'd probably opt for one of the kestrel pics personally, but curious to hear what others say.</li>
        </ul>

From the edit history, it looks like the article was created on January 15, 2021?, and then an expansion beginning on May 19, 2021 (not May 20 where the article currently is located on the DYK nom page). Assuming that is the case (unless you moved the article into main space from a user page), a character count shows that the article's prose has not been expanded sufficiently. The character count before expansion was 1118 characters, making the target expansion count 5,590 characters. The article currently has 3,874 characters which is 1,716 characters short of a 5x expansion. In the future, when you nominate an article make sure you indicate whether the article is new or expanded in the template. Also, make sure you place the article under the time stamp date of when the expansion began or the article was first created. This nomination should have been placed under May 19, not May 20. I will hold off on doing a further review until these issues are addressed. On a positive note, I enjoyed reading this article and the pictures are lovely.<a href="/wiki/User:4meter4" title="User:4meter4">4meter4</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:4meter4" title="User talk:4meter4">talk</a>) 16:45, 2 June 2021 (UTC)</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tomlinson_Hall">Tomlinson Hall</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FTomlinson_Hall&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tomlinson_Hall&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 177px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street,_Indianapolis,_Indiana,_c._1909.jpg" class="image" title="1909 Postcard of Tomlinson Hall"><img alt="1909 Postcard of Tomlinson Hall" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana%2C_c._1909.jpg/177px-Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana%2C_c._1909.jpg" decoding="async" width="177" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana%2C_c._1909.jpg/266px-Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana%2C_c._1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana%2C_c._1909.jpg/354px-Tomlinson_Hall_and_Market_Street%2C_Indianapolis%2C_Indiana%2C_c._1909.jpg 2x" data-file-width="729" data-file-height="454"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         1909 Postcard of Tomlinson Hall
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Tomlinson_Hall" title="Tomlinson Hall">Tomlinson Hall</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was inaugurated with a concert on June 2, 1886 that raised money to construct the <a href="/wiki/Soldiers%27_and_Sailors%27_Monument_(Indianapolis)" title="Soldiers' and Sailors' Monument (Indianapolis)">Soldiers' and Sailors' Monument</a> in Indianapolis?</s> <small>Source: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFSheryl_D._Vanderstel1994" class="citation book cs1">Sheryl D. Vanderstel (1994). David J. Bodenhame (ed.). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/books/edition/The_Encyclopedia_of_Indianapolis/bg13QcMSsq8C?hl=en&amp;gbpv=1&amp;dq=Tomlinson+Hall+Indianapolis&amp;pg=PA1337&amp;printsec=frontcover"><i>Tomlinson Hall</i></a>. <i>The Encyclopedia of Indianapolis</i>. <a href="/wiki/Indiana_University_Press" title="Indiana University Press">Indiana University Press</a>. p.&nbsp;1136-1137.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Tomlinson+Hall&amp;rft.pages=1136-1137&amp;rft.pub=Indiana+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.au=Sheryl+D.+Vanderstel&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.google.com%2Fbooks%2Fedition%2FThe_Encyclopedia_of_Indianapolis%2Fbg13QcMSsq8C%3Fhl%3Den%26gbpv%3D1%26dq%3DTomlinson%2BHall%2BIndianapolis%26pg%3DPA1337%26printsec%3Dfrontcover&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span>)</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that Indianapolis's <b><a href="/wiki/Tomlinson_Hall" title="Tomlinson Hall">Tomlinson Hall</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was destroyed by fire on January 30, 1958, allegedly after a pigeon dropped a lit cigarette on the roof of the building? <small>Source:
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFDawn_Mitchell2013" class="citation book cs1">Dawn Mitchell (October 28, 2013). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.indystar.com/story/news/history/retroindy/2013/10/28/retroindy-tomlinson-hall/3289059/"><i>RetroIndy: Tomlinson Hall was the gathering place for Indianapolis</i></a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Indianapolis_Star" title="The Indianapolis Star">The Indianapolis Star</a></i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=RetroIndy%3A+Tomlinson+Hall+was+the+gathering+place+for+Indianapolis&amp;rft.date=2013-10-28&amp;rft.au=Dawn+Mitchell&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.indystar.com%2Fstory%2Fnews%2Fhistory%2Fretroindy%2F2013%2F10%2F28%2Fretroindy-tomlinson-hall%2F3289059%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

Nominated by <a href="/wiki/User:4meter4" title="User:4meter4">4meter4</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:4meter4" title="User talk:4meter4">talk</a>) at 13:16, 23 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> New and long enough, within policy, Earwig finds no copyvios, QPQ done, image is public domain. ALT1 fact checks out and is more interesting. Original hook isn't supported by the source; it says the building dedication was part of the music festival, but not that the festival was actually held in the building. Good to go. <a href="/wiki/User:Antony-22" title="User:Antony-22">Antony–<i><b>22</b></i></a> (<sup><a href="/wiki/User_talk:Antony-22" title="User talk:Antony-22">talk</a></sup>?<sub><a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Antony-22" title="Special:Contributions/Antony-22">contribs</a></sub>) 05:30, 28 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nine_in_a_row">Nine in a row</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FNine_in_a_row&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nine_in_a_row&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 114px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel,_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg" class="image" title="Jock Stein, Celtic's manager in the 1960s"><img alt="Jock Stein, Celtic's manager in the 1960s" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel%2C_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg/114px-Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel%2C_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg" decoding="async" width="114" height="172" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel%2C_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg/171px-Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel%2C_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel%2C_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg/228px-Trainer_Jock_Stein_van_Celtic_in_het_Hiltonhotel%2C_Bestanddeelnr_924-3395.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2429" data-file-height="3674"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <a href="/wiki/Jock_Stein" title="Jock Stein">Jock Stein</a>, Celtic's manager in the 1960s
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that 14 seasons elapsed between the first <b><a href="/wiki/Nine_in_a_row" title="Nine in a row">run of nine consecutive titles</a></b> in Scottish football by <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> ending and the second run by <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a> starting – and that was also the gap between its end and the third run by Celtic? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rsssf.com/tabless/scotchamp.html">Scotland - List of Champions</a>, <a href="/wiki/RSSSF" title="RSSSF">RSSSF</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>: ... that prior to winning their first of <b><a href="/wiki/Nine_in_a_row" title="Nine in a row">nine consecutive titles</a></b> in the <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_Scottish_Division_One" title="1965–66 Scottish Division One">1965–66 season</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> had not been champions of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_League" title="Scottish Football League">Scottish Football League</a> for 12 years? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rsssf.com/tabless/scotchamp.html">Scotland - List of Champions</a>, <a href="/wiki/RSSSF" title="RSSSF">RSSSF</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_21"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_21">Articles created/expanded on May 21</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 21">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gang_of_25">Gang of 25</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FGang_of_25&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gang_of_25&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 129px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Margaret_Thatcher_(1981).jpg" class="image" title="Thatcher in 1981"><img alt="Thatcher in 1981" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Margaret_Thatcher_%281981%29.jpg/129px-Margaret_Thatcher_%281981%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="129" height="151" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Margaret_Thatcher_%281981%29.jpg/194px-Margaret_Thatcher_%281981%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Margaret_Thatcher_%281981%29.jpg/258px-Margaret_Thatcher_%281981%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="606" data-file-height="709"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Thatcher in 1981
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in 1981 it was feared that <b><a href="/wiki/Gang_of_25" title="Gang of 25">25 Conservative members of parliament</a></b> would vote against <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>'s economic policies and cause a split in the party? <small>"Now Thatcher's personal papers for 1981, released on Saturday, show how close the Conservative party came to splitting in the face of "brutal in-fighting" in Thatcher's inner circle, and the apparently unstoppable rise of the newly founded Social Democratic party ... the threat of revolt from a group labelled by Thatcher's inner circle as the "gang of 25" has not come to light before." from: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFTravis2011" class="citation news cs1">Travis, Alan (30 December 2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/uk/2011/dec/30/thatcher-battled-cabinet-wets-national-archives">"Thatcher battled cabinet 'wets' over Howe austerity plans"</a>. <i>The Guardian</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Guardian&amp;rft.atitle=Thatcher+battled+cabinet+%27wets%27+over+Howe+austerity+plans&amp;rft.date=2011-12-30&amp;rft.aulast=Travis&amp;rft.aufirst=Alan&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.theguardian.com%2Fuk%2F2011%2Fdec%2F30%2Fthatcher-battled-cabinet-wets-national-archives&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that despite being a suspected member of the <b><a href="/wiki/Gang_of_25" title="Gang of 25">Gang of 25</a></b> that threatened to vote against the British government in 1981, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Patten" title="Chris Patten">Chris Patten</a> was later appointed to <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>'s cabinet? <small>"it is believed that Jim Lester, Richard Needham, Chris Patten &amp; John Wheeler made up the remainder of the 'Group of 25'." from: 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.margaretthatcher.org/document/114228">"Conservative Party: "Gang of 25" letter to Chief Whip"</a>. <i>Margaret Thatcher Foundation</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">17 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Margaret+Thatcher+Foundation&amp;rft.atitle=Conservative+Party%3A+%22Gang+of+25%22+letter+to+Chief+Whip&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.margaretthatcher.org%2Fdocument%2F114228&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span> and "Secretary of State for Environment, Department for the Environment, 24 July 1989 - 28 November 1990" from: 
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://members.parliament.uk/member/1136/career">"Parliamentary career for Lord Patten of Barnes"</a>. <i>MPs and Lords - UK Parliament</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">18 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=MPs+and+Lords+-+UK+Parliament&amp;rft.atitle=Parliamentary+career+for+Lord+Patten+of+Barnes&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fmembers.parliament.uk%2Fmember%2F1136%2Fcareer&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Amy_Vilela">Amy Vilela</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FAmy_Vilela&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amy_Vilela&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Amy_Vilela" title="Amy Vilela">Amy Vilela</a></b> became an advocate for <a href="/wiki/Single-payer_healthcare" title="Single-payer healthcare">single-payer healthcare</a> after her daughter died after being turned away from a hospital for lacking health insurance?</li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: 4th QPQ out of 7 from <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/1935_New_York_anti-lynching_exhibitions" title="Template:Did you know nominations/1935 New York anti-lynching exhibitions">Template:Did you know nominations/1935 New York anti-lynching exhibitions</a></li>
        </ul>

      <h4><span id="Pieces_of_a_Woman.2C_Kata_W.C3.A9ber"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pieces_of_a_Woman,_Kata_Wéber">Pieces of a Woman, Kata Wéber</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FPieces_of_a_Woman&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pieces_of_a_Woman&amp;action=history">Pieces of a Woman</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kata_W%C3%A9ber&amp;action=history">Kata Wéber</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> moved to Berlin to write the play that would become <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i>, avoiding her husband and daughter? 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> wrote <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i>, inspired by her own experience with pregnancy loss, after <a href="/wiki/Korn%C3%A9l_Mundrucz%C3%B3" title="Kornél Mundruczó">her husband</a> found her notes about it?</li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> initially didn't want to write the story of <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i>, based on her own pregnancy loss, as she felt it was too personal?</li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> tried to get her Hungarian-language screenplay for <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i> made, but it was only picked up by American producers?</li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> spoke with psychiatrists and bereaved mothers while writing <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i>?</li> 
         <li><b>ALT5</b>:... that screenwriter <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> has said that the themes of isolation in film <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i>, about baby loss, can be relevant during the COVID-19 pandemic?</li> 
         <li><b>ALT6</b>:... that screenwriter <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> did not think that her 30-page labor scene in <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i> would be shot as a continuous take, which became the film's signature?</li> 
         <li><b>ALT7</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Kata_W%C3%A9ber" title="Kata Wéber">Kata Wéber</a></b> has written <i><b><a href="/wiki/Pieces_of_a_Woman" title="Pieces of a Woman">Pieces of a Woman</a></b></i> in Hungarian, Polish, and English?</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/500_Queer_Scientists" title="Template:Did you know nominations/500 Queer Scientists">500 Queer Scientists</a></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: <i>Pieces of a Woman</i> GA, Kata Wéber new. 2nd QPQ is <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Archie,_Marry_Me" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Archie, Marry Me">Archie, Marry Me</a>. Alts 3 and 7 (about languages) might be too implicit in the articles, but there is mention in sources used in Wéber's article so these could be stated explicitly if needed. If a reviewer doesn't like the hooks, I can propose separate ones&nbsp;:)</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_22">Articles created/expanded on May 22</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 22">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture_of_Sudan">Architecture of Sudan</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FArchitecture_of_Sudan&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Architecture_of_Sudan&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 202px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005(2).jpg" class="image" title="Nubian pyramids in Sudan"><img alt="Nubian pyramids in Sudan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005%282%29.jpg/202px-NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="202" height="97" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005%282%29.jpg/303px-NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005%282%29.jpg/404px-NubianMeroePyramids30sep2005%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="796" data-file-height="382"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Nubian pyramids in Sudan
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that the heavily protected fortress of <a href="/wiki/Buhen" title="Buhen">Buhen</a>, built around 1860 BCE by <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egyptians</a>, is one of the earliest examples for the <b><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Sudan" title="Architecture of Sudan">architecture of Sudan</a></b>?</s> <small>Source: "It is known for its large fortress, probably constructed during the rule of Senusret III around 1860 BCE (12th Dynasty). Its fortifications included a moat three meters deep, drawbridges, bastions, buttresses, ramparts, battlements, loopholes, and a catapult.")</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>: <s>... that one of the landmarks of the colonial <b><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Sudan" title="Architecture of Sudan">architecture of Sudan</a></b>, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Nile_Road_and_Railway_Bridge" title="Blue Nile Road and Railway Bridge">Blue Nile Road and Railway Bridge</a>, opened in 1909, is one of the oldest bridges still in use in <a href="/wiki/Khartoum" title="Khartoum">Khartoum</a>?</s> <small>Source: ...the first bridges spanning the Nile. (The Blue Nile Bridge opened in 1909..) </small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:<s>... <a href="/wiki/Kobar_Prison" title="Kobar Prison">Kobar Prison</a>, one of the oldest buildings of the colonial <b><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Sudan" title="Architecture of Sudan">architecture of Sudan</a></b>, was built in 1903 and is still in use today?</s> <small>Source: In Khartoum North, a large prison, today called Kobar prison and still in use, was established in 1903 ...</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:<s>... the building for the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Sudan" title="National Assembly of Sudan">Sudan's National Assembly</a> is an example of 20th century <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">brutalist</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Sudan" title="Architecture of Sudan">architecture of Sudan</a></b>?</s> <small>Source:the National Assembly building was designed in the style of brutalist architecture, and "reminiscent of classical temple architecture".</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that distinctly <a href="/wiki/Nubian_pyramids" title="Nubian pyramids">Nubian pyramids</a> <i>(pictured)</i> were built in the early history of the <b><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Sudan" title="Architecture of Sudan">architecture of Sudan</a></b>? <small>Source:Cultural relations with Sudan's northern neighbour of Ancient Egypt, with which it shared long historical periods of mutual influence, brought about both Egyptian as well as distinctly Nubian settlements with temples and pyramids.</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Obviously, the image only relates to ALT4, but could be preferable to attract more attention than the other hooks. On the other hand, I prefer any other hook about more modern architecture.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>
