      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Traveling_Man">The Traveling Man</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThe_Traveling_Man&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Traveling_Man&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 171px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:One_of_three_settings_in_an_art_installation_called_%22Traveling_Man%22_in_Deep_Ellum,_a_neighborhood_composed_largely_of_arts_and_entertainment_venues_near_downtown_in_Old_East_Dallas,_Texas_LCCN2014632793.tif" class="image" title="The Traveling Man"><img alt="The Traveling Man" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/One_of_three_settings_in_an_art_installation_called_%22Traveling_Man%22_in_Deep_Ellum%2C_a_neighborhood_composed_largely_of_arts_and_entertainment_venues_near_downtown_in_Old_East_Dallas%2C_Texas_LCCN2014632793.tif/lossy-page1-171px-thumbnail.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="171" height="114" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/One_of_three_settings_in_an_art_installation_called_%22Traveling_Man%22_in_Deep_Ellum%2C_a_neighborhood_composed_largely_of_arts_and_entertainment_venues_near_downtown_in_Old_East_Dallas%2C_Texas_LCCN2014632793.tif/lossy-page1-257px-thumbnail.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/One_of_three_settings_in_an_art_installation_called_%22Traveling_Man%22_in_Deep_Ellum%2C_a_neighborhood_composed_largely_of_arts_and_entertainment_venues_near_downtown_in_Old_East_Dallas%2C_Texas_LCCN2014632793.tif/lossy-page1-342px-thumbnail.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <i>The Traveling Man</i>
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Traveling_Man" title="The Traveling Man">The Traveling Man</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> was commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dallas Area Rapid Transit">Dallas Area Rapid Transit</a> (DART) to replace murals that were destroyed for the construction of <a href="/wiki/DART_Light_Rail" title="DART Light Rail">DART Light Rail</a> in <a href="/wiki/Deep_Ellum,_Dallas" title="Deep Ellum, Dallas">Deep Ellum, Dallas</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.dallasnews.com/news/curious-texas/2018/08/06/whats-the-story-of-the-traveling-man-in-deep-ellum-curious-texas-takes-a-stroll/"><i>Dallas Morning News</i></a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the fictional <a href="/wiki/Origin_story" title="Origin story">origin story</a> of <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Traveling_Man" title="The Traveling Man">The Traveling Man</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> is that it was a <a href="/wiki/Steam_locomotive" title="Steam locomotive">steam locomotive</a> buried beneath an <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">elm tree</a> that sprang to life when a <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> musician spilled <a href="/wiki/Gin" title="Gin">gin</a> on the tree's roots? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.dallasnews.com/news/curious-texas/2018/08/06/whats-the-story-of-the-traveling-man-in-deep-ellum-curious-texas-takes-a-stroll/"><i>The Dallas Morning News</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.slate.com/blogs/atlas_obscura/2015/04/17/dallas_traveling_man_statues_tell_the_freewheeling_tale_of_a_magic_robot.html"><i>Slate</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.dallasobserver.com/arts/5-things-you-might-not-know-about-deep-ellum-like-church-of-scientology-10455502"><i>Dallas Observer</i></a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Traveling_Man" title="The Traveling Man">The Traveling Man</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> is made of <a href="/wiki/Brushed_metal" title="Brushed metal">brushed</a> and polished sheets of <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> that are held together with approximately 10,000 stainless steel <a href="/wiki/Rivet" title="Rivet">rivets</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.slate.com/blogs/atlas_obscura/2015/04/17/dallas_traveling_man_statues_tell_the_freewheeling_tale_of_a_magic_robot.html"><i>Slate</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dallas.culturemap.com/news/city-life/08-21-14-brad-oldham-traveling-man-sculpture-trashed-deep-ellum/#slide=0"><i>CultureMap Dallas</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.dmagazine.com/publications/d-magazine/2009/september/see-this-now-the-traveling-man-series-in-deep-ellum/"><i>D Magazine</i></a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

Of course <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AGF" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:AGF">WP:AGF</a> applies but with two other hooks that are just as interesting, I'd say go with one of those. Nice work <a href="/wiki/User:Michael_Barera" title="User:Michael Barera">Michael Barera</a>!<br><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://copyvios.toolforge.org/?lang=en&amp;project=wikipedia&amp;oldid=1024538654&amp;action=search&amp;use_engine=1&amp;use_links=1">copyvios clears</a>. <a href="/wiki/User:N8wilson" title="User:N8wilson">N8</a> 17:15, 29 May 2021 (UTC) </p>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Little_Island_at_Pier_55">Little Island at Pier 55</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FLittle_Island_%28Hudson_River%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Little_Island_at_Pier_55&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 251px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Little_Island_Panorama_(50236511951).jpg" class="image" title="Little Island panorama"><img alt="Little Island panorama" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Little_Island_Panorama_%2850236511951%29.jpg/251px-Little_Island_Panorama_%2850236511951%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="251" height="78" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Little_Island_Panorama_%2850236511951%29.jpg/377px-Little_Island_Panorama_%2850236511951%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Little_Island_Panorama_%2850236511951%29.jpg/502px-Little_Island_Panorama_%2850236511951%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7181" data-file-height="2228"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Little Island panorama
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s>... that the new <b><a href="/wiki/Little_Island_at_Pier_55" title="Little Island at Pier 55">Little Island</a></b> park in New York City <i>(pictured)</i> sits on 132 pots and cost $260 million?</s> <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.6sqft.com/nycs-newest-park-little-island-finally-opens-on-the-hudson-river/">Gannon, Devin (May 20, 2021). "NYC's newest park Little Island finally opens on the Hudson River". 6sqft. </a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:<s>... that the newly completed <b><a href="/wiki/Little_Island_at_Pier_55" title="Little Island at Pier 55">Little Island at Pier 55</a></b> park in New York City <i>(pictured)</i> had been canceled in 2017, only to be revived after just 43 days?</s> <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/10/25/nyregion/diller-island-revived-cuomo.html">Bagli, Charles V. (October 25, 2017). "'Diller Island' Is Back From the Dead". The New York Times.</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:<s>... that <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Durst" title="Douglas Durst">Douglas Durst</a>, who financed lawsuits against the <b><a href="/wiki/Little_Island_at_Pier_55" title="Little Island at Pier 55">Little Island</a></b> park, claimed the park's promoter <a href="/wiki/Barry_Diller" title="Barry Diller">Barry Diller</a> said he wished Durst had been killed by his own brother?</s> <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://apnews.com/article/cdfab70905d148a0bbe35144d60c70c8">"Futuristic NY pier project pits billionaire vs billionaire". AP NEWS. July 23, 2017. </a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:<s>... that New York City parkgoers, booking reservations for <b><a href="/wiki/Little_Island_at_Pier_55" title="Little Island at Pier 55">Little Island at Pier 55</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, caused Little Island's website to crash on its opening day on May 21?</s> <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://gothamist-client.prod.nypr.digital/arts-entertainment/photos-explore-little-island-nycs-luxurious-new-floating-park-hudson">https://gothamist-client.prod.nypr.digital/arts-entertainment/photos-explore-little-island-nycs-luxurious-new-floating-park-hudson</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Little_Island_at_Pier_55" title="Little Island at Pier 55">Little Island at Pier 55</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, a new artificial island park in New York City, was described as being "in the theatrical vein of 18th century English garden follies"? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/20/arts/little-island-barry-diller.html">https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/20/arts/little-island-barry-diller.html</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_23"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_23">Articles created/expanded on May 23</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 23">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mae_Eleanor_Frey">Mae Eleanor Frey</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMae_Eleanor_Frey&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mae_Eleanor_Frey&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in 1905, <b><a href="/wiki/Mae_Eleanor_Frey" title="Mae Eleanor Frey">Mae Eleanor Frey</a></b> was the first woman to be ordained in the <a href="/wiki/American_Baptist_Churches_USA" title="American Baptist Churches USA">American Baptist Churches USA</a>? <small>Source: Fulthorp, Deborah L. (2020). "Mae Eleanor Frey: Early 20th-century Pentecostal Matriarch". In <i>Claiming Notability for Women Activists in Religion</i>, Colleen D. Hartung, ed., p. 5</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Mae_Eleanor_Frey" title="Mae Eleanor Frey">Mae Eleanor Frey</a></b> wrote <i>The Minister</i> (1939) and <i>Altars of Brick</i> (1943), in which she used narrative fiction to present the ethical and theological issues of her time, and to attack <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>? <small>Source: Qualls, Joy E. A. (2018). <i>God Forgive Us for Being Women: Rhetoric, Theology, and the Pentecostal Tradition</i>, pp. 1-2</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/In_His_Own_Write" title="Template:Did you know nominations/In His Own Write">Template:Did you know nominations/In His Own Write</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Figureskatingfan" title="User:Figureskatingfan">Figureskatingfan</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Figureskatingfan" title="User talk:Figureskatingfan">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 18:20, 24 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> This article is new enough, long enough, and within policy. The hook fact is verifiable to the cited source. I prefer the first hook, but either could be used.<a href="/wiki/User:4meter4" title="User:4meter4">4meter4</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:4meter4" title="User talk:4meter4">talk</a>) 23:51, 31 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mary_Custis_Lee">Mary Custis Lee</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMary_Custis_Lee&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 140px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:LEE,_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_(sq_cropped).jpg" class="image" title="Mary Custis Lee"><img alt="Mary Custis Lee" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/LEE%2C_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_%28sq_cropped%29.jpg/140px-LEE%2C_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_%28sq_cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/LEE%2C_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_%28sq_cropped%29.jpg/210px-LEE%2C_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_%28sq_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/LEE%2C_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_%28sq_cropped%29.jpg/280px-LEE%2C_MARY_CUSTIS_LCCN2016866128_%28sq_cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2621" data-file-height="2621"></a>

         Mary Custis Lee
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Mary_Custis_Lee" title="Mary Custis Lee">Mary Custis Lee</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, a daughter of the Confederate General <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a>, refused to sit in the "<a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">Whites only</a>" area? <small>Source: "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://boundarystones.weta.org/2013/06/13/mary-custis-lee-challenges-streetcar-segregation">arrested on June 13th in Alexandria for riding in the back of a streetcar with her black maid, having refused to move to the whites-only section at the front of the car</a>"</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Women_in_Red/Meetup/197" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Women in Red/Meetup/197">WIR edithon theme number 197 is Marys</a>, feel free to improve the hook or suggest another</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 124px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg" class="image" title="Moore pitching with the Tampa Bay Rays in 2012."><img alt="Moore pitching with the Tampa Bay Rays in 2012." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg/124px-Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="124" height="159" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg/186px-Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg/248px-Matt_Moore_in_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2637" data-file-height="3385"></a>

      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was once gifted a baseball glove belonging to <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> pitcher <b><a href="/wiki/Matt_Moore_(baseball)" title="Matt Moore (baseball)">Matt Moore</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.orlandosentinel.com/sports/os-rays-cuban-national-team-havana-20160322-story.html">"He gave Obama, a White Sox fan, a glove owned by Moore."</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Matt_Moore_(baseball)" title="Matt Moore (baseball)">Matt Moore</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> threw the first ever pitch for the <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green_Hot_Rods" title="Bowling Green Hot Rods">Bowling Green Hot Rods</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bgdailynews.com/sports/1st-hot-rod-promoted-to-tampa/article_89fcfbc5-5b6c-5ea4-8658-a2d16fb3af51.html">"Moore was part of the inaugural Bowling Green Hot Rods team in 2009, starting the first game in franchise history."</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that in 2016, <b><a href="/wiki/Matt_Moore_(baseball)" title="Matt Moore (baseball)">Matt Moore</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> came within one out of pitching a <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitter</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.si.com/mlb/2016/08/26/matt-moore-giants-dodgers-no-hitter-update">"Giants lefthander Matt Moore came within one out of a no-hitter against the Dodgers on Thursday night, only to lose his bid for history after 8 2/3 innings in San Francisco's 4-0 win."</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSegne_du%2C_Maria&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

      <ul>
       <li><s>... that "<b><a href="/wiki/Segne_du,_Maria" title="Segne du, Maria">Segne du, Maria</a></b>", requesting <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary</a> to bless her child in life and death, was written by Corduly Wöhler on 31 May 1870, and finally made it to the common <i><a href="/wiki/Gotteslob" title="Gotteslob">Gotteslob</a></i> hymnal in 2013?</s> <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.volksmusik-archiv.de/vma/files/holzapfel/11_lieder_s_bis_v.pdf">[28]</a> for the date, and others</small></li>

       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Asfaw_Yemiru" title="Asfaw Yemiru">Asfaw Yemiru</a></b><span class="nowrap">'s</span> school educated over 120,000 Ethiopian students?</li>

      <h4><span id="Three_Obliques_.28Walk_In.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_Obliques_(Walk_In)">Three Obliques (Walk In)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThree_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Three_Obliques_(Walk_In)_(Cardiff),_May_2021_07.jpg" class="image" title="Three Obliques (Walk In) in Cardiff, May 2021"><img alt="Three Obliques (Walk In) in Cardiff, May 2021" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29_%28Cardiff%29%2C_May_2021_07.jpg/162px-Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29_%28Cardiff%29%2C_May_2021_07.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29_%28Cardiff%29%2C_May_2021_07.jpg/243px-Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29_%28Cardiff%29%2C_May_2021_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29_%28Cardiff%29%2C_May_2021_07.jpg/324px-Three_Obliques_%28Walk_In%29_%28Cardiff%29%2C_May_2021_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <i>Three Obliques (Walk In)</i> in Cardiff, May 2021
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hepworth" title="Barbara Hepworth">Barbara Hepworth</a> instructed people to "<b><a href="/wiki/Three_Obliques_(Walk_In)" title="Three Obliques (Walk In)">walk in</a></b>" to her sculptures? <small>Source: "In 1962 Hepworth gave an interview to The Studio magazine in which she remarked on her interest in the abstract form and its potential appeal to viewers: 'It is easy now to communicate with people through abstraction, and particularly so in sculpture since the whole body reacts to its presence...people become themselves a living part of the work'. It is perhaps this idea which prompted her to use part of her work's titles to invite people to 'Walk In' or 'Walk Through'" ([<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.sothebys.com/en/auctions/ecatalogue/2015/beyond-limits-l15010/lot.13.html">https://www.sothebys.com/en/auctions/ecatalogue/2015/beyond-limits-l15010/lot.13.html</a> Sotheby's - Beyond Limits: The Landscape of British Sculpture 1950-2015 - Lot 13 Dame Barbara Hepworth DBE THREE OBLIQUES (WALK IN))</small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Lisl_Goldarbeiter" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Lisl Goldarbeiter">Lisl Goldarbeiter</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon">Saint George Killing the Dragon</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FSaint_George_Killing_the_Dragon&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 111px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image" title="Saint George Killing the Dragon by Bernat Martorell"><img alt="Saint George Killing the Dragon by Bernat Martorell" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/111px-Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="111" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/167px-Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/222px-Bernat_Martorell_-_Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3783" data-file-height="6001"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <i><a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon" title="Saint George Killing the Dragon">Saint George Killing the Dragon</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Bernat_Martorell" title="Bernat Martorell">Bernat Martorell</a>
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <i><b><a href="/wiki/Saint_George_Killing_the_Dragon" title="Saint George Killing the Dragon">Saint George Killing the Dragon</a></b></i> <i>(pictured)</i> was once placed at the center of the altar in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>'s chapel that was dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Saint_George" title="Saint George">Saint George</a>? <small>Source: "Conceived in the elegant, decorative International Gothic style, the painting was originally the center of an altarpiece dedicated to Saint George that was apparently made for the chapel of the palace of the Catalan government in Barcelona." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.artic.edu/artworks/15468/saint-george-and-the-dragon">Art Institute Chicago</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/St._George%27s_Basilica,_Prague" title="Template:Did you know nominations/St. George's Basilica, Prague">St. George's Basilica, Prague</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Naval_Artillery_Volunteers">Royal Naval Artillery Volunteers</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRoyal_Naval_Artillery_Volunteers&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Naval_Artillery_Volunteers&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 162px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg" class="image" title="An 1873 depiction of RNAV members"><img alt="An 1873 depiction of RNAV members" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg/162px-Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg" decoding="async" width="162" height="121" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg/243px-Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg/324px-Rn_artillery_volunteers_HMS_president_1873.jpg 2x" data-file-width="537" data-file-height="400"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         An 1873 depiction of RNAV members
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Artillery_Volunteers" title="Royal Naval Artillery Volunteers">Royal Naval Artillery Volunteers</a></b> were "not really wanted" by the Royal Navy and were disbanded less than 20 years after their 1873 founding? <small>" "The Royal Naval Artillery Volunteers (R.N.A.V.) existed from 1873 until 1892 but was not really wanted by the Navy" from: 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFLilley2012" class="citation cs2">Lilley, Terrence Dawson (June 2012), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://gala.gre.ac.uk/id/eprint/9397/1/Terence_Dawson_Lilley_2012.pdf"><i>Operations of the Tenth Cruiser Squadron: A Challenge for the Royal Navy and its Reserves</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> (PhD thesis), University of Greenwich, p.&nbsp;97</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Operations+of+the+Tenth+Cruiser+Squadron%3A+A+Challenge+for+the+Royal+Navy+and+its+Reserves&amp;rft.pages=97&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Greenwich&amp;rft.date=2012-06&amp;rft.aulast=Lilley&amp;rft.aufirst=Terrence+Dawson&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fgala.gre.ac.uk%2Fid%2Feprint%2F9397%2F1%2FTerence_Dawson_Lilley_2012.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATemplate+talk%3ADid+you+know%2FApproved" class="Z3988"></span></small></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>

         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Wilder_Brigade_Monument" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Wilder Brigade Monument">Template:Did you know nominations/Wilder Brigade Monument</a></li>

      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FGrace_Welsh&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that pianist and composer <b><a href="/wiki/Grace_Welsh" title="Grace Welsh">Grace Welsh</a></b> turned down becoming president of the <a href="/wiki/American_Conservatory_of_Music" title="American Conservatory of Music">American Conservatory of Music</a> due to thinking that it would get in the way of her teaching music?</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lynching_of_Leonard_Woods">Lynching of Leonard Woods</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FLynching_of_Leonard_Woods&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lynching_of_Leonard_Woods&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <b><a href="/wiki/Lynching_of_Leonard_Woods" title="Lynching of Leonard Woods">Leonard Woods</a></b>, a Black miner accused of killing a white mine foreman from a prominent family, was possibly lynched to prevent a trial that could have tainted the reputation of the foreman and his family? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/41320297">"'Never Thot This Could Happen In The South': The Anti-Lynching Advocacy of Appalachian Newspaper Editor Bruce Crawford"</a>, Alexander S. Leidholdt; <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Appalachian Journal">Appalachian Journal</a> 38.2/3 (2011): 198-232</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Lynching_of_Leonard_Woods" title="Lynching of Leonard Woods">Lynching of Leonard Woods</a></b> took place on the platform from which days before <a href="/wiki/US_Route_23" class="mw-redirect" title="US Route 23">US Route 23</a>, connecting Virginia and Kentucky, had been ceremoniously opened? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/41320297">"'Never Thot This Could Happen In The South': The Anti-Lynching Advocacy of Appalachian Newspaper Editor Bruce Crawford"</a>, Alexander S. Leidholdt; <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Appalachian Journal">Appalachian Journal</a> 38.2/3 (2011): 198-232</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Wises_Landing,_Kentucky" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Wises Landing, Kentucky">Template:Did you know nominations/Wises Landing, Kentucky</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Drmies" title="User:Drmies">Drmies</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Drmies" title="User talk:Drmies">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 15:13, 28 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><b>Review</b>. The article is new enough and long enough. The article is cited throughout with the hooks inline. Earwig copyvio doesn't like the long quote in the legacy section but the quote is properly attributed so no problem. QPQ is done. Alt0 is preferred. <a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Desertarun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Desertarun (page does not exist)">Desertarun</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Desertarun" title="User talk:Desertarun">talk</a>) 15:46, 29 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="23_Beekman_Place">23 Beekman Place</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2F23_Beekman_Place&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=23_Beekman_Place&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 115px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:McClintic_and_Cornell_House,_New_York_City,_NY.jpg" class="image" title="23 Beekman Place"><img alt="23 Beekman Place" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/McClintic_and_Cornell_House%2C_New_York_City%2C_NY.jpg/115px-McClintic_and_Cornell_House%2C_New_York_City%2C_NY.jpg" decoding="async" width="115" height="172" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/McClintic_and_Cornell_House%2C_New_York_City%2C_NY.jpg/173px-McClintic_and_Cornell_House%2C_New_York_City%2C_NY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/McClintic_and_Cornell_House%2C_New_York_City%2C_NY.jpg/230px-McClintic_and_Cornell_House%2C_New_York_City%2C_NY.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2583" data-file-height="3859"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         23 Beekman Place
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that architect <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudolph_(architect)" title="Paul Rudolph (architect)">Paul Rudolph</a>'s residence at <b><a href="/wiki/23_Beekman_Place" title="23 Beekman Place">23 Beekman Place</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> has a penthouse terrace overhanging the nearby street, which even Rudolph was afraid to use? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ny.curbed.com/2014/8/21/10057714/paul-rudolphs-incredible-23-beekman-relisted-for-28m">Budin, Jeremiah (August 21, 2014). "Paul Rudolph's Incredible 23 Beekman Relisted for $28M". Curbed NY.</a> </small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that architect <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudolph_(architect)" title="Paul Rudolph (architect)">Paul Rudolph</a>'s residence at <b><a href="/wiki/23_Beekman_Place" title="23 Beekman Place">23 Beekman Place</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was once described as "a remarkable composition of floating townhouses and mirrored units"? <small>Source: Stern, Robert A. M.; Fishman, David; Tilove, Jacob (2006). New York 2000: Architecture and Urbanism Between the Bicentennial and the Millennium. New York. p. 937.</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that architect <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudolph_(architect)" title="Paul Rudolph (architect)">Paul Rudolph</a>'s house at <b><a href="/wiki/23_Beekman_Place" title="23 Beekman Place">23 Beekman Place</a></b> once had an elevator without a ceiling, a translucent bathtub, and stairs without railings? <small>Source: Various</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that architect <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudolph_(architect)" title="Paul Rudolph (architect)">Paul Rudolph</a> redesigned his residence at <b><a href="/wiki/23_Beekman_Place" title="23 Beekman Place">23 Beekman Place</a></b> several times from 1961 till his death in 1997? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/1998/12/03/garden/toil-and-trouble-in-plexi-land.html">Brown, Patricia Leigh (December 3, 1998). "Toil and Trouble In Plexi-Land". The New York Times.</a> </small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT4</b>:... that within two years of buying the <b><a href="/wiki/23_Beekman_Place" title="23 Beekman Place">23 Beekman Place</a></b> house in New York City, a resident moved out after fighting with a neighbor over a brick wall? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2005/01/16/realestate/brick-walls-and-bad-blood.html">William Neuman (January 16, 2005). "Brick Walls, and Bad Blood". The New York Times.</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT5</b>:... that the stairs of architect <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rudolph_(architect)" title="Paul Rudolph (architect)">Paul Rudolph</a>'s residence at <b><a href="/wiki/23_Beekman_Place" title="23 Beekman Place">23 Beekman Place</a></b> had no railings or risers, which once scared his cleaning lady? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/1998/12/03/garden/toil-and-trouble-in-plexi-land.html">Brown, Patricia Leigh (December 3, 1998). "Toil and Trouble In Plexi-Land". The New York Times.</a> </small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>
        <ul>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_27"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_27">Articles created/expanded on May 27</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 27">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kripa">Kripa</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FKripa&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kripa&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 157px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Kripa_(crop).jpg" class="image" title="17th century painting of Kripa"><img alt="17th century painting of Kripa" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kripa_%28crop%29.jpg/157px-Kripa_%28crop%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="157" height="125" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kripa_%28crop%29.jpg/236px-Kripa_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kripa_%28crop%29.jpg/314px-Kripa_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="812"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         17th century painting of Kripa
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in <a href="/wiki/Hindu_mythology" title="Hindu mythology">Hindu mythology</a>, <b><a href="/wiki/Kripa" title="Kripa">Kripa</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was born from a clump of weeds after his father ejaculated on it? Source:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sacred-texts.com/hin/m01/m01131.htm">The Mahabharata, Book 1: Adi Parva: Sambhava Parva: Section CXXX</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">"The suddenness, however, of his mental agitation, caused an unconscious emission of his vital fluid [...] His vital fluid, however, having fallen upon a clump of heath, was divided into two parts, whence sprang two children that were twins [Kripa and Kripi]."</span> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that after the <a href="/wiki/Pandava" title="Pandava">Pandavas</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Kurukshetra_War" title="Kurukshetra War">Mahabharata War</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Kaurava" title="Kaurava">Kauravas</a>, some surviving allies of the Kauravas, including <b><a href="/wiki/Kripa" title="Kripa">Kripa</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, raided the camp of the Pandavas during their absence and massacred all the remaining warriors? Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.co.in/books?id=ivQ6CwAAQBAJ&amp;q=Keechak&amp;pg=PT105&amp;redir_esc=y#v=snippet&amp;q=Kripa%20killed&amp;f=false">Penguin Companion to the Mahabharata</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">"In the dead of night, in the absence of the PANDAVAS, Ashwathama went with KRITAVARMA and his maternal uncle KRIPA into the Pandava camp and killed the five sons of Draupadi along with DHRISTADYUMNA and SHIKHANDI".</span></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span id="Bodleian_Plate.2C_President.27s_House_.28College_of_William_.26_Mary.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bodleian_Plate,_President's_House_(College_of_William_&amp;_Mary)">Bodleian Plate, President's House (College of William &amp; Mary)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBodleian_Plate&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( Article history links: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bodleian_Plate&amp;action=history">Bodleian Plate</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=President%27s_House_%28College_of_William_%26_Mary%29&amp;action=history">President's House (College of William &amp; Mary)</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 158px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Bodleian_Plate.jpg" class="image" title="Print made with the Bodleian Plate."><img alt="Print made with the Bodleian Plate." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bodleian_Plate.jpg/158px-Bodleian_Plate.jpg" decoding="async" width="158" height="124" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bodleian_Plate.jpg/237px-Bodleian_Plate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bodleian_Plate.jpg/316px-Bodleian_Plate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1209"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Print made with the Bodleian Plate.
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Bodleian_Plate" title="Bodleian Plate">Bodleian Plate</a></b> is among the earliest depictions of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="College of William &amp; Mary">College of William &amp; Mary</a>'s campus, including the <b><a href="/wiki/President%E2%80%99s_House_(College_of_William_%26_Mary)" class="mw-redirect" title="President’s House (College of William &amp; Mary)">President's House</a></b>? <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.dailypress.com/history/dp-nws-bodleian-plate-20180920-story.html">[29]</a> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <a href="/wiki/College_of_William_%26_Mary" title="College of William &amp; Mary">College of William &amp; Mary</a>'s <b><a href="/wiki/President%27s_House_(College_of_William_%26_Mary)" title="President's House (College of William &amp; Mary)">President's House</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Wren_Building" title="Wren Building">Wren Building</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brafferton_(building)" title="Brafferton (building)">Brafferton</a> are depicted by the <b><a href="/wiki/Bodleian_Plate" title="Bodleian Plate">Bodleian Plate</a></b>? <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.dailypress.com/history/dp-nws-bodleian-plate-20180920-story.html">[30]</a></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span id="Thebaid_.28Latin_poem.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Thebaid_(Latin_poem)">Thebaid (Latin poem)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThebaid_%28Latin_poem%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Thebaid_%28Latin_poem%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Thebaid_(Latin_poem)" title="Thebaid (Latin poem)">Thebaid</a></b></i> inspired a <a href="/wiki/Middle_Irish" title="Middle Irish">Middle Irish</a> poem named <i>Togail na Tebe</i> ('Destruction of Thebes')? <small>Source: Perhaps also to be dated to some time near the millennium is the original of what has come down to us as the Middle Irish Togail na Tebe, or 'Destruction of Thebes' ... Dewar (1991) xxxix</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>: ... that, according to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Maxwell_Ogilvie" title="Robert Maxwell Ogilvie">Robert Maxwell Ogilvie</a>, the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Thebaid_(Latin_poem)" title="Thebaid (Latin poem)">Thebaid</a></b></i> "cannot be said to be about anything"? <small>Source: R. M. Ogilvie, in fact, took criticism of the 'Thebaid' to, perhaps, its ultimate low point when he declared in his 'Roman Literature and Society' (p. 292): "The 'Thebaid' cannot be said to be about anything." Ahl (1984) 2804</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Rhodesian_Independence_Bell" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Rhodesian Independence Bell">Template:Did you know nominations/Rhodesian Independence Bell</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Improved to Good Article status by <a href="/wiki/User:Modussiccandi" title="User:Modussiccandi">Modussiccandi</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Modussiccandi" title="User talk:Modussiccandi">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 15:04, 27 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p>

        </ul>

        <span class="template-ping">@<a href="/wiki/User:Valereee" title="User:Valereee">Valereee</a>:</span> thanks for the review.         <dl>
         <dd>
          <ul>
           <li><b>ALT2</b>: ... that <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a> erroneously considered the author of the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Thebaid_(Latin_poem)" title="Thebaid (Latin poem)">Thebaid</a></b></i> to have been a Christian?</li> 
           <li><b>ALT3</b>: ... that <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a> erroneously considered <a href="/wiki/Statius" title="Statius">Statius</a>, the author of the <i><b><a href="/wiki/Thebaid_(Latin_poem)" title="Thebaid (Latin poem)">Thebaid</a></b></i>, to have been a Christian?</li>
          </ul> 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <dl>
             <dd>
              <small>Source: Statius was much admired in the Middle Ages; regarded by Dante as a Christian, he appears in Cantos 21 and 22 of the Purgatorio where his spirit meets that of Virgil, appropriately enough in view of Statius' reverence for the earlier poet. Statius is represented as explaining how he was led to Christianity by certain passages in Virgil. Howatson (2011)</small>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </dd>
          </dl>
         </dd>

      <h3><span id="Articles_created.2Fexpanded_on_May_28"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Articles_created/expanded_on_May_28">Articles created/expanded on May 28</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Did_you_know/Approved&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Articles created/expanded on May 28">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="51st_Defense_Battalion">51st Defense Battalion</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2F51st_Defense_Battalion&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=51st_Defense_Battalion&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/51st_Defense_Battalion" title="51st Defense Battalion">51st Defense Battalion</a></b>, formed during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, was the first <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African American</a> unit in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a>? <small>Source:Information is taken from the table on page 28 of the following Marine Corps Publication - <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.marines.mil/Portals/1/Publications/The%20Right%20to%20Fight%20African-American%20Marines%20in%20World%20War%20II%20PCN%2019000313200_2.pdf">https://www.marines.mil/Portals/1/Publications/The%20Right%20to%20Fight%20African-American%20Marines%20in%20World%20War%20II%20PCN%2019000313200_2.pdf</a></small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rockefeller_Apartments">Rockefeller Apartments</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FRockefeller_Apartments&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rockefeller_Apartments&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 171px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg" class="image" title="Rockefeller Apartments"><img alt="Rockefeller Apartments" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg/171px-W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg" decoding="async" width="171" height="114" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg/257px-W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg/342px-W_54th_St_Mar_2021_16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Rockefeller Apartments
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Apartments" title="Rockefeller Apartments">Rockefeller Apartments</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, with its glass-enclosed cylindrical "bows", allowed 15 percent more air and natural light than other apartments of the time? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://s-media.nyc.gov/agencies/lpc/lp/1276.pdf">"Rockefeller Apartments" (PDF). New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission. June 19, 1984. p. 1, 9.</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that the <b><a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Apartments" title="Rockefeller Apartments">Rockefeller Apartments</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, designed by two architects of New York City's <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">Rockefeller Center</a>, was meant to entice tenants to the center? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://s-media.nyc.gov/agencies/lpc/lp/1276.pdf">"Rockefeller Apartments" (PDF). New York City Landmarks Preservation Commission. June 19, 1984. p. 2.</a></small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that the site of New York City's 11-story <b><a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Apartments" title="Rockefeller Apartments">Rockefeller Apartments</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was excavated in "railroad time" and the steel structure was completed within one month? <small>Source: (1) "Steel to Go Up On Rockefeller Suites in Week: Excavations Completed on 'Railroad Time' for Two West 54th St. Buildings". New York Herald Tribune. March 27, 1936. p. 36 (2) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://timesmachine.nytimes.com/timesmachine/1936/04/04/88649848.pdf">"New Rockefeller Houses Reported a Third Rented" (PDF). The New York Times. April 4, 1936. p. 32.</a> (3) "Rockefeller Apartments Reported 86% Filled". New York Herald Tribune. May 30, 1936. p. 28.</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT3</b>:... that architectural critic <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Mumford" title="Lewis Mumford">Lewis Mumford</a> once compared the ornament of New York City's <b><a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Apartments" title="Rockefeller Apartments">Rockefeller Apartments</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> to the singing of "the four-and-twenty blackbirds"? <small>Source: Mumford, Lewis (October 3, 1936). "The Sky Line: Modernity and Commerce". The New Yorker. 13: 47–51.</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz">Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FBloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 171px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg" class="image" title="Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz"><img alt="Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg/171px-The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg" decoding="async" width="171" height="115" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg/257px-The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg/342px-The_Bloody_Wednesday_Olkusz_1940.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1812" data-file-height="1215"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that while the 1940 <b><a href="/wiki/Bloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz" title="Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz">Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> affected both Poles and Polish Jews, a number of sources have incorrectly described the victims as only Jews? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.archiwum.wyborcza.pl/Archiwum/1,0,4679829,20060715KR-DLO,Yad_Vashem_sie_myli,.html">http://www.archiwum.wyborcza.pl/Archiwum/1,0,4679829,20060715KR-DLO,Yad_Vashem_sie_myli,.html</a> , <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://olkuscyzydzi.pl/wp-content/uploads/2016/10/Olkusz-Zaglada-i-pamiec.pdf">http://olkuscyzydzi.pl/wp-content/uploads/2016/10/Olkusz-Zaglada-i-pamiec.pdf</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that during the 1940 <b><a href="/wiki/Bloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz" title="Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz">Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, all male inhabitants of the town, Poles and Jews alike, were subject to hours of abuse by the German soldiers? <small>Source: virtually any source</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Norman_K._Risjord" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Norman K. Risjord">Template:Did you know nominations/Norman K. Risjord</a></li>
        </ul>

      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Piotrus" title="User:Piotrus">Piotrus</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Piotrus" title="User talk:Piotrus">talk</a>). Self-nominated at 05:21, 28 May 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><b>Review</b>. The article is new enough, long enough and well cited throughout. Copyvio is clear. QPQ is done. It is quite a shocking read - which hasn't been translated to the hooks. I can give you some ideas as starting points "on July 16 the SS arrived, gathered up 20 people and executed them" or on "July 31 Jewish inhabitants were stripped naked, stomped upon, forced to recite Christian prayers and to stone one another". Maybe you have your own reasons not for writing harsher hooks, in which case I will OK the ones above. <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Desertarun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Desertarun (page does not exist)">Desertarun</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Desertarun" title="User talk:Desertarun">talk</a>) 16:31, 28 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul> 
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <ul>
           <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Desertarun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Desertarun (page does not exist)">Desertarun</a>, I couldn't think of making this fit within the word limit, but I am open to reviewing and "adopting" any ALT hooks you could craft yourself? Regarding the 16 deaths, they were arguably not part of the Bloody Wednesday. It's a bit weird how the day that is remembered is the one with fewer casualties - maybe it's the case of collective memory, the victims of the 16th were killed, but most of the victims of the 31st survived... anyway, that's why I think the events of the 16th are a 'background' and it's harder to work them into a hook, despite arguably 20 casualties being more significant than 1-3 related to the 31st. --<sub style="border:1px solid #228B22;padding:1px;"><a href="/wiki/User:Piotrus" title="User:Piotrus">Piotr Konieczny aka Prokonsul Piotrus</a>|<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Piotrus" title="User talk:Piotrus"><span style="color:#7CFC00;background:#006400;"> reply here</span></a></sub> 04:57, 29 May 2021 (UTC)</li>
          </ul>

           <dd>

         <li><s><b>Alt2</b> ... that a photo of <b><a href="/wiki/Bloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz" title="Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz">Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i> was taken during the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Occupation of Poland">occupation of Poland</a> by Nazi Germany, and is "known to everyone in Olkusz"?</s></li> 
         <li><s><b>Alt3</b> ...that during <b><a href="/wiki/Bloody_Wednesday_of_Olkusz" title="Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz">Bloody Wednesday of Olkusz</a></b> <i>(pictured)</i>, Jewish inhabitants were stripped naked, beaten and forced to stone one another?</s></li>

            <ul>
             <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Desertarun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Desertarun (page does not exist)">Desertarun</a>, Regarding the ALTs, thank you for the ideas, but with all due respect I think mine are better. Here's why: ALT2 simply describes the picture, plus it unlikely the readers will care the photo is said to be known to everyone in the small Polish town they likely never heard of. As for ALT3, it perpetuates the incorrect description of this event as something that affected only the Jewish inhabitants of the town (reminder: out of 23 known casualties of summer 1940 in Olkusz, 1 has been identified as Jewish, 22, as far as I can tell, were gentile/ethnic Poles). --<sub style="border:1px solid #228B22;padding:1px;"><a href="/wiki/User:Piotrus" title="User:Piotrus">Piotr Konieczny aka Prokonsul Piotrus</a>|<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Piotrus" title="User talk:Piotrus"><span style="color:#7CFC00;background:#006400;"> reply here</span></a></sub> 10:34, 29 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

             <dd>

      <h4><span id="Ka.CA.BBelepulu_Pond"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ka?elepulu_Pond">Ka?elepulu Pond</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FKa%CA%BBelepulu_Pond&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ka%CA%BBelepulu_Pond&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <p><s>* ... that the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">United States Army Corps of Engineers</a> chose not to assert the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_to_roam" title="Freedom to roam">public's right to access</a> <b><a href="/wiki/Ka%CA%BBelepulu_Pond" title="Ka?elepulu Pond">Ka?elepulu Pond</a></b> after the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">United States Supreme Court</a> ruled that it did not apply to a similar pond nearby? <small>Source: <a href="/wiki/The_Honolulu_Advertiser" title="The Honolulu Advertiser">The Honolulu Advertiser</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78516893/the-honolulu-advertiser/">"Corps Awaits Ruling on Kaelepulu Pond"</a></small></s> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that <b><a href="/wiki/Ka%CA%BBelepulu_Pond" title="Ka?elepulu Pond">Ka?elepulu Pond</a></b>, formerly a 200- to 400-acre <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Hawaiian_aquaculture" title="Ancient Hawaiian aquaculture">Hawaiian fish pond</a>, is now about 95 acres and <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">polluted</a> after having been partially filled in for a housing development? <small>Source: First part <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1061/40976(316)444">here</a> on the first page, second part <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.civilbeat.org/2019/09/where-a-developer-sees-houses-enchanted-lake-sees-a-wetland-to-protect/">here</a> about halfway down</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Ester_Wajcblum" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Ester Wajcblum">Ester Wajcblum</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>

      <h4><span id="Priest-king_.28sculpture.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Priest-king_(sculpture)">Priest-king (sculpture)</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FPriest-king_%28sculpture%29&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Priest-king_%28sculpture%29&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 123px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg" class="image" title="The Priest-king, c. 2000–1900 BCE"><img alt="The Priest-king, c. 2000–1900 BCE" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg/123px-Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg" decoding="async" width="123" height="159" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg/185px-Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg/246px-Mohenjo-daro_Priesterk%C3%B6nig.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="584" data-file-height="754"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         The <i>Priest-king</i>, c. 2000–1900 BCE
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that in 1972 <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a> made <a href="/wiki/Zulfiqar_Ali_Bhutto" class="mw-redirect" title="Zulfiqar Ali Bhutto">Zulfiqar Ali Bhutto</a> choose between the <a href="/wiki/Dancing_Girl_(sculpture)" title="Dancing Girl (sculpture)"><i>Dancing Girl</i></a> and the <b><a href="/wiki/Priest-king_(sculpture)" title="Priest-king (sculpture)"><i>Priest-king</i></a></b> (pictured) to be returned to <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>? <small>Source: "both the statues were initially taken away in the 1930s by John Marshall and put on display at Delhi Museum. “When [Zulfikar Ali] Bhutto tried to get back the relics, then Indian prime minister Indira Gandhi refused and told him to choose one of them,” Gadhi told The Express Tribune. “Bhutto preferred the statue of King Priest over the nude dancer.” " Tunio, Hafeez, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://tribune.com.pk/story/409184/with-king-priest-in-hiding-dancing-girl-yet-to-take-the-road-back-home">"With King Priest ‘in hiding’, Dancing Girl yet to take the road back home"</a>, 16 July 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Express_Tribune" title="The Express Tribune">The Express Tribune</a></i> </small></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: coming</li> 
         <li><i>Comment</i>: Original version was largely copyvio, by a now-blocked sockpuppet. The statue is an important one, so I have taken it over.</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><small>Created by <a href="/wiki/User:Johnbod" title="User:Johnbod">Johnbod</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Johnbod" title="User talk:Johnbod">talk</a>) and <a href="/wiki/User:Aglrochisat" title="User:Aglrochisat">Aglrochisat</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Aglrochisat" title="User talk:Aglrochisat">talk</a>). Nominated by <a href="/wiki/User:Johnbod" title="User:Johnbod">Johnbod</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Johnbod" title="User talk:Johnbod">talk</a>) at 03:27, 5 June 2021 (UTC).</small> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/File:Symbol_confirmed.svg" class="image"><img alt="Symbol confirmed.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/16px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/24px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Symbol_confirmed.svg/32px-Symbol_confirmed.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="185"></a> Jumping on this so I have a QPQ in pocket for a later date... Whether we call it a new creation or an expansion, it easily qualifies length-wise. I see no issues with remaining CV, the sourcing is solid, and the tone is NPOV. The hook is interesting and tempts the reader to click not only on the bolded article but also the <i>Dancing Girl</i> link as well, which I love. No issues with the source or the content of the hook, and the length is fine. Confirmed by archive.org that the image was legitimately released as CC in 2006, it is used in the article and looks nice even at a small size. As soon as the QPQ is done, this is good to go. ?<a href="/wiki/User:Premeditated_Chaos" title="User:Premeditated Chaos">PMC</a>? <a href="/wiki/User_talk:Premeditated_Chaos" title="User talk:Premeditated Chaos">(talk)</a> 04:16, 5 June 2021 (UTC)</li>
        </ul>
       </dd>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Angel_with_Golden_Hair">The Angel with Golden Hair</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FThe_Angel_with_Golden_Hair&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Angel_with_Golden_Hair&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <div class="dyk-img" style="float: right; margin-left: 0.5em;"> 
       <div class="thumbinner mp-thumb" style="background: transparent; border: none; padding: 0; max-width: 124px;"> <a href="/wiki/File:Goldenlocks.jpg" class="image" title="The Angel with Golden Hair by an unknown Russian artist"><img alt="The Angel with Golden Hair by an unknown Russian artist" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Goldenlocks.jpg/124px-Goldenlocks.jpg" decoding="async" width="124" height="157" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Goldenlocks.jpg/186px-Goldenlocks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Goldenlocks.jpg/248px-Goldenlocks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="466" data-file-height="590"></a>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="padding: 0.25em 0; word-wrap: break-word;">
         <i><a href="/wiki/The_Angel_with_Golden_Hair" title="The Angel with Golden Hair">The Angel with Golden Hair</a></i> by an unknown <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> artist
        </div>
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that <i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Angel_with_Golden_Hair" title="The Angel with Golden Hair">The Angel with Golden Hair</a></b></i> is one of <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>'s oldest <a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">icons</a>? <small>Source: "Dating from before the Mongol invasion, this is one of the oldest surviving Russian icons." <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://artsandculture.google.com/asset/the-angel-with-golden-hair/WwGXFbBcbfJquA?hl=en">Google Arts &amp; Culture</a></small></li>
      </ul>

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h4><span id="Mo.CA.BBolelo"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mo?olelo">Mo?olelo</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FMo%CA%BBolelo&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mo%CA%BBolelo&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that some <b><a href="/wiki/Mo%CA%BBolelo" title="Mo?olelo">mo?olelo</a></b> took multiple days to tell in full, and were sometimes told in the form of <a href="/wiki/Hula" title="Hula">hula</a>? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/4139042">Hä, Mana, Leo</a> page 88: "Tradition tells us that while some of our great epics took days to recount, audiences were enthusiastic recipients of our ancestral mo'olelo, especially when they took the form of hula"</small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that after the 1896 ban of the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian language</a> for instruction in the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii" title="Territory of Hawaii">Territory of Hawaii</a>'s schools, generations of <a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiians" title="Native Hawaiians">Hawaiians</a> were unable to read <b><a href="/wiki/Mo%CA%BBolelo" title="Mo?olelo">mo?olelo</a></b> that hadn't been translated to English? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/stable/23540867">N? Hulu Kupuna</a> pages 43-44: "the ancestors of today's K?naka Maoli [...] wrote mo?olelo [...] this has been obscured [...] Much of this ignorance resulted from the banning, in 1896, three years after the illegal overthrow of Queen Lili?uokalani, of Hawaiian language as a medium of instruction in Hawaii's private and public schools. Among the devastating effects were that several generations of K?naka Maoli [...] could not understand, speak, read, or write in the language of their parents or grandparents. [...] many, if not most, students in Hawaiian language and Hawaiian studies are familiar with the work of only five or six authors, and that is because those authors' works have been translated into English."</small></li> 
         <li><b>ALT2</b>:... that the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii" title="Territory of Hawaii">Territory of Hawaii</a>'s 1896 ban of the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">Hawaiian language</a> for instruction in schools obscured the history of <b><a href="/wiki/Mo%CA%BBolelo" title="Mo?olelo">mo?olelo</a></b>? <small>Source: same as ALT1</small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
         <li><i>Reviewed</i>: <a href="/wiki/Template:Did_you_know_nominations/Marja_Kuba%C5%A1ec" title="Template:Did you know nominations/Marja Kubašec">Marja Kubašec</a></li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="KIXL">KIXL</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FKIXL&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KIXL&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li><s> ... that Christian radio station <b><a href="/wiki/KIXL" title="KIXL">KIXL</a></b> near <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a>, canceled an <a href="/wiki/Anti-pornography_movement_in_the_United_States" title="Anti-pornography movement in the United States">anti-pornography</a> program for its graphic depiction of gay sex? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78575203/anti-porn-radio-show-pulled-after-sex/">https://www.newspapers.com/clip/78575203/anti-porn-radio-show-pulled-after-sex/</a></small></s></li>
      </ul>

Is there a source to state that the previously daily show stopped completely? Otherwise we can rephrase the hook to say "pulled off air" or something; a QPQ has been carried out. My preference would be for the lead to be longer, but not a major hold-up, once the cancellation is clarified I have no issues with this nomination - <a href="/wiki/User:Dumelow" title="User:Dumelow">Dumelow</a> (<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Dumelow" title="User talk:Dumelow">talk</a>) 08:56, 30 May 2021 (UTC)</li>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FM_extended_band_in_Brazil">FM extended band in Brazil</span></h4> 
      <div class="plainlinks hlist"> 
       <ul>
        <li>( <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template%3ADid_you_know_nominations%2FFM_extended_band_in_Brazil&amp;action=edit">Review or comment</a></li> 
        <li><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=FM_extended_band_in_Brazil&amp;action=history">Article history</a> )</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <ul>
       <li>... that Brazil has <b><a href="/wiki/FM_extended_band_in_Brazil" title="FM extended band in Brazil">extended its FM broadcasting band</a></b> to allow AM radio stations to move to FM, even in major urban centers? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.frontliner.com.br/migracao-de-emissoras-am-para-fm-usara-frequencias-fora-da-faixa-fm/">https://www.frontliner.com.br/migracao-de-emissoras-am-para-fm-usara-frequencias-fora-da-faixa-fm/</a></small> 
        <ul>
         <li><b>ALT1</b>:... that in May 2021, ten radio stations were the first in Brazil to begin broadcasts in a <b><a href="/wiki/FM_extended_band_in_Brazil" title="FM extended band in Brazil">new extended FM band</a></b> below the existing frequencies? <small>Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.gov.br/mcom/pt-br/noticias/2021/maio/mcom-entrega-certificado-as-emissoras-que-estreiam-a-faixa-estendida-da-fm">https://www.gov.br/mcom/pt-br/noticias/2021/maio/mcom-entrega-certificado-as-emissoras-que-estreiam-a-faixa-estendida-da-fm</a></small></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul>

       <dd>
        <ul>

         <li>Article is new enough (created 29 May) and long enough (2,349 characters of prose).</li> 
         <li>Article is neutral and contains sufficient inline citations. Earwig <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://copyvios.toolforge.org/?lang=en&amp;project=wikipedia&amp;title=FM_extended_band_in_Brazil">finds no copyvio issues</a>.</li> 
         <li>Both hooks are neutral and of adequate length, and both are cited inline in the article. IMO ALT1 is less interesting and more wordy, so I prefer ALT0. However, I think ALT0 itself could be snappier if it were shortened to simply: 
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <b>ALT2</b>: ... that Brazil has <b><a href="/wiki/FM_extended_band_in_Brazil" title="FM extended band in Brazil">extended its FM broadcasting band</a></b> to allow AM radio stations to move to FM?
           </dd>
          </dl></li> 
         <li>QPQ is done.</li>

Not all of the migrating stations are going on the extended band. I could see ALT2 working if it were worded "to allow <b>more</b> AM radio stations to move to FM" (emphasis mine for demonstration). <a href="/wiki/User:Sammi_Brie" title="User:Sammi Brie"><span style="color:#f06292">Sammi Brie</span></a> (she/her •&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/User_talk:Sammi_Brie" title="User talk:Sammi Brie">t</a> • <a href="/wiki/Special:Contributions/Sammi_Brie" title="Special:Contributions/Sammi Brie">c</a>) 00:26, 1 June 2021 (UTC)
